Current Events Commentary

British Diplomacy and Pacific Security

— Yu

The diplomatic policies of the nations related to the Pacific are still extremely chaotic. Because national politicians are not God; they cannot say, like God, "Let there be light," and there is light. National politicians are also not like soldiers. Treaties they painstakingly conclude over years are often destroyed by soldiers in an instant. This era is one of destruction, not creation. This is true in Europe and in the Pacific. The two largest militaristic countries in Europe—Germany and Italy—have transformed from enemies at daggers drawn to bosom buddies. They will clearly sing a duet in the upcoming drama of total war. Britain's Baldwin and France's Léon Blum want to drag these two tigers out of their unconstrained wilderness and back into the old prison of Locarno. This is a foolish fantasy, a waste of effort with no results.

The high and low atmospheric pressure of European politics not only concerns Europe itself but also affects the politics of the Far East. We know that in Asia, there is a country that not only has a secret agreement with Germany, which is stirring up trouble in Europe, but also plays things by ear. When the atmospheric pressure of European politics is high, it temporarily suspends its activities. Once the atmospheric pressure is low, knowing that European countries are preoccupied with their own disputes and have no time to look eastward, or that some countries with a direct stake in the Far East, such as Britain, even have to rely on it for guidance on Far Eastern affairs, it chimes in with its allies in the same camp and actively launches attacks on the Asian continent. Haven't we seen this play out over the past five years?

From the above, we can get a general understanding that peace is indivisible. There will be no peace in the Pacific without world peace. Those who advocate limiting war to one corner while keeping themselves out of the vortex of war are either foolish or have ulterior motives. If the major powers presiding over the League of Nations, such as Britain and France, had cooperated with the United States, as the U.S. Secretary of State suggested at the time, and strictly adhered to the covenant, implementing sanctions to deter the aggressor, then the Abyssinian affair might not have happened. The authority of the League of Nations might not have been lost to this extent. The Far Eastern situation might not have deteriorated to this degree. And the Washington Nine-Power Treaty and the Kellogg-Briand Pact might not have become waste paper, as they are today. "A single misstep leads to complete failure." Now, national politicians want to maintain world peace by patching up the many treaties that have already been pierced by bayonets, but it is probably too late. The most obvious example is the recent Pacific Conference in Yosemite, USA, where the Japanese representative Yoshizawa publicly argued for amending the Nine-Power Treaty, citing the "necessity of expanding into China" as the reason. He also stated that including words like "sanctions" in the revised treaty would make Japan feel "uneasy." It is clear that the concept of "collective security" has not only been erased in fact but even the idea itself has been rejected by countries that use military occupation as a means of territorial expansion. In such circumstances, how can there be peace in the world?

Since the concept of "collective security" has faded due to the arrogance of the aggressor nations and the loss of prestige of the League of Nations, the open diplomacy stipulated in the League of Nations covenant, which requires "all international treaties to be notified to the League of Nations and published by the League of Nations," will inevitably disappear due to the incompetence of the League of Nations. The prevalence of secret diplomacy, as in the old days, is naturally unavoidable today.

Britain, which has the power to influence world politics, has been under the control of the Conservative Party in recent years. In Europe, it initially called for collective security, but ultimately revealed its embarrassing and ugly true face in the Italian-Abyssinian affair. In the Pacific, from beginning to end, it has taken seeking practical benefits as its starting point. As the newly appointed British Ambassador to China, Archibald Clark Kerr, said in Tokyo, "Britain's interests in China are primarily economic in nature, especially trade." Therefore, we can summarize Britain's current foreign policy toward China as how to maintain its trade interests in the face of another country's ambition to swallow the whole of China. They know that in this turbulent time in Europe, they do not have the strength to compete with the emerging power in East Asia alone. Therefore, their policy is to seek compromise as long as their existing interests are not excessively damaged. According to the Tokyo Asahi Shimbun of the 2nd of last month, Ambassador Clark Kerr met with the Japanese Ambassador to Britain, Yoshida, in London and exchanged detailed opinions on Japan's political, economic, and military intentions toward China and Britain's hopes and intentions toward China. He also strongly advocated the necessity of cooperation between Britain and Japan in the Far East. Foreign Minister Eden completely agreed. Although this is one-sided propaganda from the Japanese, it is probably not far from the truth. From this, we can understand why Rose had to go through Japan first to come to China and why Rose had to go to Tokyo again before leaving China. And why did Ambassador Clark Kerr have to visit the Tokyo government first before coming to China this time? From Britain's perspective, this kind of diplomacy may allow it to preserve some of its trade interests temporarily. However, the facts of the past five years tell us that under the so-called "leapfrog" process, the boundaries of British trade have already been squeezed and confined to the Yangtze River basin. In this situation, if they still avoid the open road of peace and cling to the husk of realism, I am afraid that when the flames spread, Britain's situation in the Far East will be even more embarrassing than the Italian-Abyssinian affair.

Rosenberg's Speech

Goebbels' Speech

Then Propaganda Minister Goebbels took the stage to speak. His wording was generally the same as Rosenberg's. Final Act of Russian Military Maneuvers Performance of Airborne Transportation of Troops Swift Movements Leave Observers Speechless

(Moscow) Today was the last day of the Soviet Russian Red Army's large-scale maneuvers held in Minsk, between Moscow and Berlin. In the final act, 1,200 soldiers, carrying parts for 18 cannons and 150 machine guns, simultaneously jumped from airplanes, parachuting to the ground. It is said that the Soviet Russian maneuvers were extremely mechanized. Four Soviet Russian army generals observed the maneuvers in person. (Moscow) In the Soviet Russian Red Army's large-scale maneuvers, an air force battle is now being staged. Many high-speed bombers, fighters, and warplanes are participating. The Legislative Yuan Meeting Revises and Passes the Municipal Autonomy Law and Passes the Regulations for Reorganizing Guangdong's Financial Public Debt

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan opened its 71st meeting at 11 a.m. on the 11th. Sixty-four members were present. The newly appointed members present were Ye Xiasheng, Feng Ziyou, Lin Gengbai, Aisha. The rest were absent. Sun Ke chaired the meeting, and Liang Hancao was the secretary. Matters discussed: (1) The draft general budget for local ordinary income and expenditure for Ningxia Province in the 24th year of the Republic of China. It was resolved that although the case could not fully comply with the statutory standards of the local budget law, because the province belonged to a border area and was a poor province with a short history of construction, the case was passed as it was. The budget for the next year should reduce military and police expenses as appropriate, and increase education, culture, industry, construction, transportation, justice, and other expenses as much as possible, and reduce the tax rate and surtax on land in order to meet the purpose of teaching, raising, and gathering the people, and to lighten the burden on the people. The income and expenditure of the case were each listed at more than 3.6 million yuan. (2) The case of the ordinary income and expenditure budget for the additional 23rd year of the Republic of China in Hubei Province was resolved and passed. The income and expenditure were each listed at more than 340,000 yuan, and the name of a subject listed in the case was revised. (3) The general budget for local ordinary income and expenditure in Hubei Province for the 24th year of the Republic of China was resolved and passed as it was. The income and expenditure were each listed at more than 20.39 million yuan. The following two points should be improved in the next year: (1) The budget of Wuhan City should be included in the provincial budget in accordance with the methods of Wuchang and Yichang cities. (2) The income of Yichang and other items should be fully included in accordance with the example of Wuhan City. 4. Revised Appendix 2 to the National Assembly Representative Election Law, various cases of counties under the jurisdiction of the third and second districts of Jiangsu Province. It was resolved that the counties listed in the third district of Jiangsu in Appendix 2 to the National Assembly Representative Election Law should be changed to be listed in the fourth district, and the counties listed in the fourth district should be changed to be listed in the third district. (5) Revised the Implementation Law of the County Autonomy Court. (6) Revised the Municipal Autonomy Law. (7) Revised the Implementation Law of the Municipal Autonomy Law. It was resolved that the above three cases should be passed in accordance with the review and amendment proposal of the Autonomy Law Committee. (8) The case of the Regulations and Amortization Table for Reorganizing Guangdong's Financial Public Debt in the 25th year of the Republic of China was resolved and passed with amendments. (Central News Agency dispatch, 11th)

(Nanjing) The Regulations for Reorganizing Guangdong's Financial Public Debt in the 25th year of the Republic of China, passed by the Legislative Yuan on the 11th, are as follows: Article 1. In order to reorganize Guangdong's finances and enrich the preparation of mill receipts, the National Government issues public debt, named the Regulations for Reorganizing Guangdong's Financial Public Debt in the 25th year of the Republic of China. Article 2. The fixed amount of this public debt is 120 million yuan in national currency. Article 3. This public debt is scheduled to be issued on October 1, 1936. Article 4. The interest rate of this public debt is set at 4% per annum, with interest paid twice a year on March 31 and September 30. Article 5. The term of this public debt is set at 30 years, with principal repaid twice a year on March 31 and September 30. The principal will be repaid at 3% per annum for the first 20 years and 4% per annum for the last 10 years. By September 30, 1966, the principal and interest will be fully repaid. The foregoing repayment of principal shall be carried out by lottery. Article 6. The funds for the principal and interest of this public debt shall be allocated from the collection of consolidated taxes in the Guangdong area. The Ministry of Finance shall order the Tax Affairs Department to allocate the amount of principal and interest due each time on a monthly average to the account of this public debt under the National Debt Fund Management Committee in the Central Bank for storage and payment in accordance with the provisions of the Amortization Table. Article 7. The Central Bank is designated to manage the repayment of principal and interest of this public debt. Article 8. The face value of this public debt is divided into four types: 10 yuan, 100 yuan, 1,000 yuan, and 10,000 yuan, all of which are unregistered. Article 9. This public debt ticket may be freely bought, sold, and mortgaged. When a security deposit must be paid for official business, it may be used as a substitute and may also be used as a guarantee reserve for banks. Article 10. Those who commit forgery and damage the credit of this public debt shall be punished by the judicial organs according to law. Article 11. These regulations shall be implemented from the date of promulgation. (Central News Agency dispatch, 11th)

(Nanjing) The case of the Regulations for Reorganizing Guangdong's Financial Public Debt in the 25th year of the Republic of China was carefully studied during the review process in the Legislative Yuan. Ma Yinchu, chairman of the Finance Committee of the Yuan, reported on the review process of the case at the Yuan meeting on the 11th, stating that the purpose of the Ministry of Finance's issuance of public debt for reorganizing Guangdong's finances was originally to compensate for the shortage of preparations for mill receipts in Guangdong Province, so as to stabilize the credit of mill receipts, and then gradually seek to reorganize and implement legal tender. However, when the committee initially reviewed the case, it was unanimously believed that the exchange rate of mill dollars used in Guangdong Province was unstable compared with the current legal tender. Even if the preparation was made up and the price was stabilized, it would still be necessary to find another way to unify the finances in the future. It would be better to take this opportunity to make a fundamental reorganization, issue legal tender, and recover mill receipts, which would not only kill two birds with one stone, but also achieve twice the result with half the effort. Therefore, at that time, both parties had slightly different opinions on the reorganization of Guangdong's finances. Later, when the committee held its second meeting to review the case, representatives of the Ministry of Finance came to the Yuan to explain again that there were difficulties in adopting radical measures in the political, economic, and financial aspects of reorganizing Guangdong's finances. The committee members also unanimously sympathized and completed the review according to the original plan. Whether it is appropriate or not, please have the Yuan meeting approve it. After the words were finished, all the commissioners had no objection, and the case was successfully passed. (Central News Agency dispatch, 11th)

(Nanjing) At the meeting of the Legislative Yuan on the 11th, the Municipal Autonomy Law and the County and Municipal Autonomy Law, which were passed by the Third Session of the Eighth-Sixth Meeting of the previous winter, were further revised based on the principles of local autonomy laws and regulations promulgated by the Central Government and by referring to the revised situation of the County Autonomy Law. After the revision, the Municipal Autonomy Law is still divided into nine chapters: the establishment of the city, the autonomous matters of the city, the citizens of the city, the citizens' congress, the city council, the municipal government, the city's financial district, and the supplementary provisions, totaling 68 articles, which is two articles less than the original proposal. The main points of the revision are to abolish the original "Lu Lin" in the organization of the districts under the city and change it to "Bao Jia". Ten households form a "Jia", and a "Jia" head is established. Ten "Jia" form a "Bao", and a "Bao" head is established. Ten or more "Bao" form a "District", and the rest are the same as the original plan. As for the Implementation Law of the County and Municipal Autonomy Law after the revision, the former has 17 articles and the latter has 16 articles. Except for the addition of "The county may, due to its geographical area, population, economy, culture, and other special circumstances, submit a report to the superior agency for approval to guide autonomous affairs by districts", the rest are only textual modifications. (Central News Agency dispatch, 11th)

Letter

Letter from Lü Liangchen: Respected Editor, I read in your newspaper on September 2nd that I, along with Bai Jianwu and Zheng Yanhou, were recruiting soldiers to send to eastern Suiyuan to aid the border trouble, etc. On September 17th, 1935, I was appointed by Chairman Shang of the Hebei Provincial Government as the Director of the Tangshan Public Security Bureau. On June 4th, 1936, I resigned and handed over the post. I was appointed as a city government counselor by the Beiping Municipal Committee in Beiping and have not gone elsewhere. I took leave to return to my hometown on September 1st. I do not know who I have offended, fabricating facts and slandering my reputation. Your newspaper is known for its just and upright commentary. I earnestly request a correction. I would be most grateful. Furthermore, I do not know the rebels Bai and Zheng. I will never do anything unreasonable or illegal. Sincerely,

To Shenbao, Lü Liangchen, September 5th.

Yellow River Floodwaters Receding Slowly, Middle and Lower Reaches of Shandong Still Mostly Dangerous; Luokou Water Level Continues to Rise; Kong Xiangrong Inspects Lower Reaches

Jinan Communication: The flood in the Yellow River at Shanzhou has passed. Lisheng Village in the upstream of this province has begun to recede since the day before yesterday. However, the middle and lower sections not only have not fallen, but have increased. The water level at Luokou, a dozen miles north of Jinan City, was 31.1 meters at 8:00 p.m. last night. Today (the 10th), it rose to 31.15 meters at 6:00 a.m. and 31.21 meters at 2:00 p.m., with a continuing upward trend. The highest recorded water level at Luokou was 31.4 meters in 1933. It has not reached this figure in the past two years. Based on this year's situation, it is feared that it may break the 31.4-meter mark. This abnormal phenomenon of upstream decline and downstream increase is mainly due to the blockage of the estuary, hindering discharge. Kong Xiangrong, chairman of the Yellow River Conservancy Commission, decided to request 1.2 million yuan from the central government to purchase four dredgers and start dredging the estuary next spring. He also plans to build a stone dam at the estuary. Kong himself led Wu Nankai, the chief engineer of the commission, from Jinan to the estuary downstream this morning to inspect and design. The River Affairs Bureau considers Luokou to be the gateway to the provincial capital. The rising water level in recent days is feared to be dangerous. Last night, the bureau selected ten staff members from each department, led by Zhao Youzeng, the chief of the audit section, to be stationed in the upper and lower sections of Luokou to direct the laborers in defense. Zhao Luren, the chief of the general affairs section, also went to inspect the various sections of Luokou this morning. Fortunately, the south bank is very high and is entirely stone坝 (embankment/dam), which is relatively solid. Coupled with the discharge in the middle of the river, it should be safe. This morning, the south bank embankment was submerged by 1.56 to 2 meters of water. The north bank is low, almost level with the water. If it rises further, there may be a danger of overflowing. The turbulent waves in the river are拍浮 (lapping/splashing) against both banks. The water roaring under the iron bridge is like thunder, audible for miles. The masts of the ships are also visible for miles beyond the堤 (embankment/dike). The residents' temporary straw sheds on the river滩 (beach/bank) have been moved to the embankment. There is a car码头 (wharf/pier) at Gaijiagou below Luokou to transport cars across the river by boat. Currently, due to the high water, the码头 (wharf/pier) has been submerged. The small boats carrying passengers on both banks are also finding it difficult due to the high water. It takes two hours to cross from this bank to the other bank. According to river workers, if the溜 (current/flow) does not change, the water level at Luokou will not be a major problem even if it rises further. However, there is always a danger of抽刷 (erosion/scouring) when the water recedes, which cannot be ignored.

Yang Yongtai Discusses Methods for Reviving Rural Hubei; Striving to Improve Varieties, Provide Storage and Inspection, Effectively Organize Baotou, Establish Various Cooperatives, and Train District Administration Personnel as the Backbone for Promoting Rural Administration

Hankou Communication: Hubei Province has had a bumper harvest of rice and wheat this year, which has not been seen in more than a decade. The cotton production also ranks third in the country. After years of natural disasters and man-made calamities, the bankrupt rural areas have received deep relief, not only bringing joy to the countryside but also to the markets. Fearing that low grain prices would harm farmers, the provincial government has put forward opinions, requesting the Executive Yuan to pay close attention. At the same time, taking advantage of this opportunity, it has promoted the "Six Modernizations" policy and is actively promoting the recovery of rural areas, seeking fundamental reforms. To understand the content of this plan, this newspaper reporter visited Yang Yongtai, chairman of the provincial government, who told us about the methods for reviving rural areas, which are recorded on the left:

Methods for Reviving Rural Areas

Yang said that in recent years, the entire rural area of our country has tended to go bankrupt, and Hubei is no exception. Not only have there been years of disasters, but many farmers have had to fill their stomachs with grass roots, tree bark, and观音土 (kaolin). Even if they occasionally have a bumper harvest, low prices and low grain prices harm farmers, so that although they can barely make a living through hard work all year round, they still cannot afford to buy clothes. As a result,歉 (deficiency) becomes a disaster, and abundance also becomes a disaster. This is due to the lack of adjustment in the entire national economy, and the failure to effectively improve agriculture itself is a major factor. Now, the first slogan for improving agriculture in Hubei is "Agricultural Scientification" and "Agricultural Industrialization." Our country is based on agriculture, but purely agricultural products, such as rice, wheat, cotton, tobacco, sugar, flour, and agricultural manufactured products, are imported from abroad every year, with a value of over 600 million yuan, which is disheartening. Hubei produces approximately 2 to 3 million dan of cotton each year, ranking third in the country, which cannot be said to be insignificant. However, foreign cotton still flows in continuously because the quality of cotton is poor. Therefore, foreign cotton must still be used to spin 25-count yarn. To make domestic cotton sell well, it is necessary to improve cotton varieties and strictly prohibit adulteration with water and other substances. The rice and wheat themselves also need to be improved. We must pay attention to water conservancy and use new agricultural tools. With selection, fertilization, weeding, and pest control, using some science, agricultural production will naturally increase. The government, on the other hand, will set up warehouses for storage, set up bureaus for inspection, improve the quality, strictly set standards, and improve rural financial organizations. In the future, domestic production and sales can be expected to meet supply and demand, and the import of舶来品 (imported goods) will not be difficult to stop. As for the farmers' working time, they are only busy with farming for 120 days a year, and the remaining nine months are spare time. Farmers' labor can be used to develop other industries. It is best to engage in rural side businesses, such as gardening, fruit trees, vegetables, flower cultivation, animal husbandry, horses, cattle, sheep, pigs, chickens, ducks, bees, fish, etc. In terms of handicrafts, such as brewing土酒 (local wine), making soy sauce, ginning cotton, spinning, weaving, paper making, and engaging in藤工 (rattan work),蓆工 (mat work), bamboo编 (weaving), and 麻制 (hemp products). They can also use lakes and swamps to catch fish and pick lotus, and use mountainous areas to plant forests and hunt. These side businesses only require farmers' labor, which is farmers' capital, which can greatly help the revival of rural areas. The second slogan is "Rural Baotouization" and "Rural Cooperatization." Because farmers have shallow knowledge and stubborn ideas, it is necessary to have a practical organization to promote agricultural scientification and agricultural industrialization. In politics, it is the organization of baotou, and in economics, it is the establishment of various cooperatives. These are the two most important organizations in rural areas. It can also be said that cooperation is the economic baotou of rural areas, and blood baotou is the political cooperation of rural areas. A well-managed baotou system can not only maintain治安 (public security) in a passive way, but also actively promote all construction projects. The various cooperatives have many conveniences. With credit cooperatives, farmers can use funds. With utilization cooperatives, those who need to purchase new tools or materials related to production due to improved farming or agricultural product processing, which one person cannot afford, can jointly invest, purchase, and operate through utilization cooperatives to increase production. With consumer and sales cooperatives, farmers can purchase and sell daily necessities and agricultural products directly to the market without being manipulated by merchants. These various cooperatives must be established one by one in rural areas. The third slogan is "Farmer Groupization" and "Farmer Training." On the one hand, they participate in壮丁队 (strong-arm teams),保安队 (security teams), and义勇队 (volunteer corps). On the other hand, they jointly manage afforestation, road construction, flood prevention, drought prevention, and various construction projects. By only using labor and not spending money, they can achieve the goal of increasing production. In the future, we will implement the proposed slogans in a practical manner.

Personnel for Promoting Rural Administration

The reporter further asked about the organizations and personnel for promoting the Six Modernizations policy. Yang said that people call the county magistrate the people-loving official, but in reality, the county magistrate does not have many opportunities to contact the people. To promote rural administration, district chiefs and district staff must be used because district chiefs are in the countryside and their every move directly affects the general public. Their position is not only the ears and eyes of the county magistrate but also the leader of rural construction. The联保 (joint guarantee) directors and联保 (joint guarantee) secretaries of each township are the cadres of rural construction who are connected with each other. Therefore, the district chief is also the pivot for connecting the upper and lower levels and bears the major responsibility for rural construction. In response to this need, the province has already set up district offices, which will soon cover the entire province. The training of district administration personnel has now been carried out to the third term. The purpose of district administration training is to enable district administration personnel to develop both文武兼修 (literary and martial arts) and to be both君师并作 (rulers and teachers), using "管 (management), 教 (education), 养 (nurturing), 卫 (protection)" to address the root causes of the people's "散 (scattered), 愚 (ignorant), 贫 (poor), 弱 (weak)" and thoroughly cure them. There are currently four problems with administrative personnel: first, compromise, accommodation, and perfunctoriness; second, inertia, lethargy, lack of energy, and lack of motivation; third, embellishment and hypocrisy; and fourth, waste and squandering. I encourage district administration personnel to adopt four-干 (doing/working) spirits, that is, to use "硬干 (hard work)" to cure compromise and accommodation, "快干 (fast work)" to cure inertia and lethargy, "实干 (practical work)" to cure embellishment and hypocrisy, and "苦干 (hardship work)" to cure waste and squandering. If district administration personnel can adopt this spirit of砥砺 (encouragement) and practice, then the success of district administration lies here, and the revival of rural areas also lies here. (September 10th)

Rampant Bandits in Zhangzhou Prefecture, Fujian; Raiders Operate in Small Groups, Inflicting Utterly Cruel Suffering; Farmers Face Appalling Tax Burdens

Xiamen Dispatch: Haicheng County, only forty *li* from Zhangzhou, is located on the coast at the mouth of the Jiulong River and is a wealthy area under Zhangzhou jurisdiction. After June, when bandits in southern Fujian began to stir, Haicheng also suffered from banditry. However, the bandits in Haicheng are neither like the large groups of local militia and bandits in Quanzhou Prefecture, nor like the communist bandits in western Fujian and Zhangzhou Prefecture. They are merely small groups of twenty or thirty people, yet their harm is even more severe than that of the large groups. Since late July, they have become extremely rampant, dividing into four groups: (1) the Huang Hedong group in the Shanhoushan, Xiguan, and Pi Ban areas; (2) the Huang Guotai group in the Daogang and Yuzhen Hengni areas; (3) the Hong Datou group outside the East Gate; (4) the Zheng Beizai group in Banzi. They occupy the four rural areas, and almost everything outside the county seat has become a communist-controlled area. They kidnap, plunder, kill, and maim with extreme cruelty. According to statistics, from July 20 to August 20, within one month, 34 villagers were killed, 63 were kidnapped, and 2,000 people were displaced and fled. Each of these four groups of bandits has only twenty to thirty people. Furthermore, according to a petition submitted by the Haicheng native association in Xiamen to the county government and pacification commissioner at the end of last month, "In the Haicheng area, bandits kidnap, rob, set fires, and kill dozens of times a month. The four groups, Huang Hedong, etc., each have no more than twenty or thirty people, yet in twenty days, there have been about twenty known bandit cases. Haicheng has a stationed company, a security team of forty men, a militia cadre team of sixty men, and thirty police officers, totaling more than two hundred soldiers and police, yet they allow small groups of bandits to do as they please." The petition includes a list of twenty bandit cases in two weeks. For example, the Kokeng community was attacked by bandits on the 26th, and the community leader, Lin Shigen, and four others were killed on the spot, and four people were kidnapped. Two of them were beheaded by the bandits, who sent their heads back to their families as a demonstration. This illustrates the ferocity of the bandits. At the end of August, the Haicheng County government offered rewards for the capture of the four bandit leaders: 1,000 yuan each for Huang Guotai and Huang Hedong, and 800 yuan each for Hong Datou and Zheng Beizai, with half the reward for killing them. However, the bandits have not been subdued at all. In early September, several new bandit leaders emerged: (1) Chen Jinquan, based in Lingdong; (2) Chen Lianqing, based in Lubian; (3) Gan Hai'e of Fenglin community; (4) Gan Shui of Cangli community; (5) Gan Shuzhi of Huangkang community; (6) Gan Jiangquan of Zhongcuo community; (7) Gan Baitang of Gangkou community, all with ten or more people or just a few, together with the Huang and Zheng Hong four groups, they widely distribute "black lists" in various villages. The so-called "black list" is a notice informing someone to pay a certain amount of money; if they fail to pay by the deadline, they will be kidnapped, killed, or their house will be burned. From September 2 to 7, each village was assigned between 300 and 1,000 such notices. The documented amount for those with verifiable victims and amounts is more than 28,000 yuan. The "black lists" were printed in blue ink on newspaper and bore the inscription "Third Brigade of the Fujian Provincial Independent Corps of the Chinese People's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Army" with a forged seal. As a result, there is terror in various villages, and villagers are scattering and fleeing. No one dares to harvest the rice. More than a thousand villagers near the town enter the city at night to escape the bandits and sleep in the open. In addition, the burning of houses and the theft of cattle are countless. Therefore, although the ten bandit groups in Haicheng are all small, their harm is greater than that of other counties. Furthermore, the tax burden on the villagers of Haicheng is extremely heavy. In addition to temporary levies and the purchase of firearms, as well as the extraction of one to three *dou* of unhusked rice after each *dou* of planted crops is harvested, the known tax items include: Baojia expenses, local gazetteer office expenses, anti-superstition donations, Baozhang office expenses, director office expenses, militia cadre team expenses, a certain cadre team bullet expenses, cadre team soldier subsidies, patrol expenses, patrol bullet expenses, patrol soldier subsidies, county Baojia expenses, district office telephone expenses, training expenses, county government messenger miscellaneous expenses, security team bullet expenses, aircraft donations, police uniform expenses, stationed troops' house repair expenses, district office house repair expenses, sports expenses, district men's salary expenses, deficit expenses, second civilian labor expenses, Bao Lian establishment expenses, registration certificate fees, militia roster fees, Bao Lian special expenses, district team leader salary expenses. These are 29 items. The above only refers to the common burdens on farmers; other temporary and commercial taxes are not included. Therefore, there is now a saying in Haicheng about three things that are abundant: bandits are abundant, taxes are abundant, and refugees are abundant. (September 11)

Details of the Murder of Japanese Resident Nakano in Haibu, Guangdong; The Deceased Had Been in China for Over Twenty Years and Was a Local Expert in Beihai; The Japanese Consulate Will Send Personnel to Investigate the Truth of the Incident

Guangzhou Dispatch: The murder of Japanese resident Junzo Nakano occurred on the 3rd of this month in the port of Beihai, Guangdong Province. This matter has been reported in various telegrams in recent days. Local news suggests that Nakano either committed suicide out of anger or provoked trouble by arguing with locals. The Japanese Consulate in Guangzhou received news of the incident on the 8th. As Consul-General Nakamura had gone to Shanghai the previous week on official business, the consulate has not yet made any statement. Deputy Consul Seichiku Sadaharu has only sent a secretary and notified the Guangdong Provincial Government of the case, as well as reporting to the Japanese Embassy in China and planning to send personnel to the scene to investigate the truth of the matter. According to news from Beihai, the murdered Japanese man, Junzo Nakano, was 52 years old. He came to the port of Beihai over twenty years ago and opened a "Maruichi" pharmacy, also selling Japanese-made children's toys and other sundries. Over the years, his business was doing well, so Nakano married a local woman in Beihai and had children. Later, he took a concubine and also had children. Nakano has resided in Beihai for over twenty years, and through constant exposure, he has become a local expert in Beihai. He speaks the Beihai dialect just like a local, and few know that he is a foreigner. Nakano's life was comfortable. In addition to doing business, he often traveled to the interior of Guangdong, venturing deep into remote forests and occasionally going to rural villages. Although locals secretly guarded against these personal activities, he relied on foreign power for protection, so they could do nothing about it. Recently, as Nakano was familiar with local conditions and relied on the authority of a foreigner, he often interfered excessively in local public affairs, and local people's feelings towards him deteriorated. On the afternoon of the 3rd, several locals entered the Maruichi pharmacy, intending to buy eyeglasses. Because they could not agree on the price, Nakano came out. It is unknown how, but he argued with the customers, and then they started fighting. Nakano was no match and was stabbed by the visitors, suffering serious injuries. After the incident, the assailants fled. By the time the police arrived, the culprits were gone. Nakano's wife went to the Beihai Public Security Bureau to report the case. The bureau immediately dispatched a large number of armed police to search for the suspects, but after searching for half the night, they still found nothing. The head of the Public Security Bureau, Chen Zhen, went to Hepu City the next day to report to the senior military officer stationed there. The authorities immediately issued orders to their subordinates to earnestly protect foreigners and to instruct the people to endure humiliation and bear the burden, and not to act rashly on emotion. After Nakano was injured that day, his son (about twenty years old, currently studying at Hepu Middle School) urgently hired Dr. Wu Shigui from the French hospital to treat him, but due to the severity of his injuries, he died soon after. After this unfortunate incident occurred, Beihai merchants were deeply afraid of diplomatic negotiations, so they suspended business and transported their inventory out of the port to ensure safety. Later, through the military and police's forceful suppression and encouragement to do business with peace of mind and not to disturb themselves, the hearts of the people in Beihai have only slightly calmed down in recent days. (September 9)

Kunshan: A Ginkgo Tree Emits Strange Light at Midnight

Behind the Samsungtan near Zhangpu Town in the sixth district of the county, there is a huge ginkgo tree, several *zhang* high, with a long history. Every summer and autumn, it blooms and bears fruit. According to local residents, starting on the 24th of last month, the top of the tree has emitted strange, colorful light every midnight, and it has not stopped yet. As a result, the news has spread far and wide, and people are marveling at it. The general villagers are extremely alarmed and plan to collect money to build a temple there, which is foolish indeed.

Suzhou: County Government Arrests Opium Smokers

County Magistrate Deng believes that there are more than 2,400 opium smokers in the county who have failed to appear for questioning. He issued summonses some days ago, but they still did not appear. Therefore, he ordered the Public Security Bureau to carry out named arrests. On October 1, a total of 108 opium smokers who failed to appear were arrested and sent to the county government yesterday (the 11th) for detention, pending investigation. Arrests continued yesterday, and more than 100 more people were arrested. However, many are avoiding arrest out of fear of punishment. The county government is determined to rigorously pursue them in order to strengthen the prohibition policy.

Wuxi: A Young Woman Commits Suicide Out of Shame and Indignation

Yun Ronggen, a resident of Dongda Street in the city, is a water worker by trade. He married a Ms. Ma and has two sons and a daughter. The daughter, named Wenxiu, is twenty years old and skilled in embroidery. She usually stays at home and observes propriety. She is engaged to Zhu Bingqing of Lianyuan Street and will marry in the winter. Chen Jiasu (also known as Ah Qi), the young master of the Wanan Pawnshop next door, falsely accused Wenxiu of having an affair with the young master of a certain money shop and falsely obtained two yuan in legal tender from Yun Ronggen in the name of it. Ronggen returned home and rebuked Wenxiu. Unexpectedly, Wenxiu, feeling compelled and helpless, secretly took opium and committed suicide the previous morning (the 10th). Rescue efforts were ineffective, and she died around 3:00 PM. Afterwards, the local Public Security Bureau and the local court sent personnel to investigate the case in order to handle it according to the law.

Yangzhou: A Seventy-Year-Old Woman Dies of Indignation

Wei Zhongyuan, a villager in Weijiadang, Zhongzha Town, Fifth District of Jiangdu, was reported by the local community leader, Shi Dequan, last year for writing threatening letters demanding money. He was arrested and sent to the court and sentenced to six months in prison. Now that he has completed his sentence and returned, his elder brother, Zhongyou, encountered Shi's father, Dayuan, on the road, and they had an argument. They argued all the way to Shi's house. Shi then went to the town office and reported that Zhong destroyed the stove and said that 32 yuan in legal tender and a small lock in the cabinet were missing. The town office prepared a document and sent Wei Zhongyou to the district office, and after questioning, he was sent to the county. Now Wei's mother (about seventy years old) is grieving that her son has been repeatedly accused and detained by the Shi family. On the night of the 8th, she went to the Shi family to explain, but she was so anxious that she collapsed and died in the Shi family's house. The Shi family was shocked at the sight and fled. When Wei's mother's family heard the news, they gathered more than a hundred women from the clan and drove to the Shi family to reason with them. It is not yet known how it will end.

Bengbu: Entertainers Request Reduction in Singing Tax

The entertainers in this port, originally called prostitutes, used to pay a singing tax of six yuan per month to the Public Security Bureau. Later, a military surcharge of four yuan was added, totaling ten yuan per month. After the Public Security Bureau abolished the tax collection office, this tax was collected by the Fengyang Business Tax Bureau. Now, the entertainer representative, Li Xiaoting, and others argue that, due to the current economic downturn and declining entertainment, the monthly tax of ten yuan for entertainers is truly beyond their means. They have specially petitioned the Anhui Finance Department to order the cancellation of the additional four yuan and to divide the singing tax into three levels of two yuan, four yuan, and six yuan in order to lighten the burden. It is not known whether this will be approved.

Local News

Social Affairs Bureau Supervises the Summoning of Factory Owners; Explains the True Meaning of Labor-Management Coordination; Bureau Director Pan, Section Chief Xu, and Others Deliver Speeches; Hope Both Parties Will Cooperate and Share the Burdens Together

According to the *Xin Sheng She*, in accordance with the resolutions of the recent joint Party-Government meeting, in order to eliminate labor unrest, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, together with the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Public Security Bureau, summoned the owners of silk factories, cotton mills, and silk weaving factories to the bureau yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM to discuss and explain the true meaning of labor-management coordination. More than twenty people attended, including Qi Yiwen of Yong'an Textile Factories 1, 2, 3, and 5, Li Xizhao, Hua Jianren of Shenxin Factories 1, 6, 8, and 9, and Zhang Peishen of Xiangcheng Heki Silk Factory. Xu Yefu, the chief of the third section of the bureau, presided over the meeting. After reporting the significance of convening the discussion meeting, he said that the occurrence of labor unrest is enough to affect governance and security, and how to prevent it in advance is appropriate. Although government agencies are responsible, industrial and commercial enterprises should also assist the government for their own interests, so that labor unrest can be eliminated in the bud.

Points to note:

1. If a factory is forced to close or suspend work for more than one month, regardless of whether the reason is due to reorganization or financial difficulties, it should be reported in advance.

2. If it is necessary to reduce a portion of workers due to cost-cutting, or if workers' performance is truly poor and they must be dismissed, it should be reported in advance.

3. Reducing wages is an unavoidable measure to maintain business during this period of weak purchasing power, but this move is most likely to cause disputes and should be reported in advance.

4. There is no problem with increasing working hours while simultaneously increasing wages, but some workers may be unwilling to work excessively due to limited physical strength. Moreover, increasing working hours without increasing wages will naturally lead to disputes, so if it is unavoidable to increase working hours, it should be reported in advance.

In short, all of the above are points to note. Any event that could cause a labor-management dispute must be reported at any time so that government agencies can have the opportunity to mediate in advance, so that various disputes can be reduced from large to small, and from existence to non-existence. Then, mediation director Wang Xianqing delivered a speech, saying that in order to achieve labor-management coordination, both spiritual and material aspects must be taken into account. Materially, such as improving treatment, etc., in this era of economic downturn, the factory may not be able to bear the burden in reality, so let's set that aside for now. As for the spiritual aspect, if the factory can deal with it properly, it can also reduce many unnecessary disputes. For example, the recent dispute at the Hongxing Sock Factory was only a verbal conflict between workers, but it caused the entire factory to stop. Fortunately, all those present are experienced and should be able to understand that the factory should treat the workers as parents in a leadership and protective role, and that passionate emotions should be deeply rooted in the lower levels, so that the spiritual and material aspects can be combined, sharing weal and woe, cooperating sincerely, and there is nothing to fear.

Bureau Director's Speech:

Finally, Bureau Director Pan delivered a speech, saying that Section Chief Xu has already conveyed the significance of convening the discussion meeting today, and everyone should understand it. Recently, the situation is tense, and all those who pay attention to the international environment are worried about the occurrence of unexpected events. Although the government is responsible for this responsibility, all sectors should work together. For example, if industrial and commercial affairs are handled improperly, it may also affect security. Especially in factories with a large number of workers, even if a small number of people stir up trouble, it can cause extreme disputes. Some factory workers have labor union organizations, while others do not. Those with organizations have the Party Headquarters to lead them, while those without organizations are easily exploited. Recently, some secret organizations have taken advantage of the opportunity to incite labor unrest in the name of saving the country. Industries such as silk factories, cotton mills, and silk weaving factories have a large number of workers, and once there is an opportunity, they will instigate them from the middle, creating a confrontational situation and using this as a pretext to cause trouble. Although military and police agencies are responsible for local security, this bureau hopes for labor-management coordination to reduce disputes, which can also maintain security. The three industries of silk factories, cotton mills, and silk weaving factories that have been convened today have many workers who are like a heap of loose sand. In addition to discussing with the Party Headquarters and the persons in charge of the labor movement to find ways to have representatives lead these workers, persuade them with reason, and explain the importance of the overall situation, it is hoped that each factory can also be mindful of the current difficulties, labor-management coordination, and cooperation. If there is a problem, it is hoped that it will be handled fairly so that disputes do not easily occur. If there is a fear that a dispute may occur, it is hoped that each factory will report to this bureau at any time, and we will do our best to persuade and find ways to quell it. I believe that everyone is concerned about the decline of the country's status and that, in order to seek the smooth development of their businesses, there is no hope of causing trouble to affect security. Any dispute that is not easily resolved is not due to the factory and the workers themselves, but often there is a third party involved with ulterior motives, attempting to disrupt order. Recently, a certain tabloid supplement had an article saying how difficult the lives of silk weaving factory workers are. This kind of talk, which does not understand the truth, is due to a lack of careful consideration. This bureau welcomes everyone to give advice at any time and hopes to communicate news at any time to assist the government in safely weathering this difficult environment so that it is not destroyed by others. After the speech, factory representatives such as Li Xizhao and Zhang Peishen contributed their opinions and then dispersed.

General Labor Union Issues Order; Trade Unions Warn Workers Not to Strike or Slow Down; Implement Labor-Management Coordination; Disputes Will Be Mediated According to Law

The Municipal General Labor Union issued General Order No. 6 yesterday, stating: In order to comply with the order, our country has been affected by the global economic downturn for years. Rural areas are bankrupt, and industry and commerce are declining. In addition, disasters are frequent, and people's purchasing power is declining. If we do not urgently seek remedies, the consequences are unthinkable. The union has repeatedly issued orders urging labor-management coordination, hoping to turn the tide. However, labor unrest in the city has been fluctuating and unstable in recent days, and the future is worrying. In addition to separately submitting reports to Party and government agencies, ordering each factory not to stop work, reduce wages, or dismiss workers at will, and sincerely advising employers in various industries, we hereby reiterate the previous order and earnestly explain that if an accident occurs, they should immediately request mediation according to law and not lightly strike or slow down work, lest they incur blame. The union has high hopes for this. This order is issued on September 11, 1936, by Chairman Zhu Xuefan and Standing Committee Members Zhou Xuexiang, Shao Xubai, Zhang Kechang, Long Peiyun, Li Mengnan, and Ye Xianggao.

Hydrographic Survey Bureau Sends Two Ships to Sound Shentan

The Shentan shoal at the mouth of the Yangtze River has been silted up, and the Dredging Bureau has dispatched a large dredging vessel to dredge it. However, the area of the shoal is very large, and it cannot be completed in a short period of time. During the dredging period, the silt near the shoal is changing again. Therefore, the Hydrographic Survey Bureau has now dispatched the surveying ships Ganlu and Jiaori to the Shentan area outside Songkou to conduct soundings and report to the Dredging Bureau at any time for reference in dredging.

Methods for Transporting and Selling Imported Goods Purchased and Stored Before the Implementation of Transport and Sales Regulations

The Nanjing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration received an order from the Ministry of Railways stating that the Ministry of Finance had issued a notice stating that recently, various chambers of commerce had sent telegrams requesting assistance for goods purchased and stored by merchants before the implementation of the regulations on inspecting the transport and sale of imported goods, so that they could obtain permits for transport and sale. It has now been stipulated that for goods purchased and stored in inland areas without customs before the implementation of the transport and sale regulations, merchants should first register with the local chamber of commerce. If they need to be transported and sold elsewhere, the chamber of commerce should verify that the goods match the registered goods and issue a storage goods transport and sale permit for transport and sale. For all imported goods that should be inspected in commercial ports and in Beijing and Jiaoji, regardless of whether they are old or new purchases, if they need to be transported and sold elsewhere, they should all present tax payment evidence to the local customs in accordance with the regulations on inspecting the transport and sale of imported goods and apply for a transport and sale permit. In addition to issuing separate orders, it is appropriate to request investigation and compliance. In addition to issuing separate orders, the bureau is hereby ordered to instruct the traffic department to comply.

Municipal Government Order Announces Provisional Measures for Boiler Inspection; All Factories with Boilers Must Register; Certificates Issued Upon Passing Inspection are Valid for One Year

The Shanghai Municipal Government instructed the Bureau of Social Affairs: A document has been presented regarding the revision of the provisional measures for boiler inspection in accordance with the order, requesting review and announcement for implementation. The document has been reviewed in its entirety and should be approved. The Bureau should immediately announce and implement it. This order, with attachments, is hereby recorded. The full text of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs' Provisional Measures for Boiler Inspection is as follows: Article 1: All factories with boilers must not use them unless they have been inspected by a legally registered mechanical engineer and a certificate of inspection is issued. Article 2: The boilers referred to in these measures include the following types of equipment: (1) Steam boilers: equipment that generates water vapor at a pressure higher than atmospheric pressure for any industrial purpose. (2) Steam containers: containers that hold water vapor at a pressure higher than atmospheric pressure for heating, boiling, baking, evaporation, or other similar purposes. (3) Compressed air containers: containers that hold compressed air. (4) Other pressure vessels: those designated by the Bureau from time to time to comply with the provisions of these measures. Article 3: Any factory that installs or modifies a boiler after the implementation of these measures must submit plans and drawings to the Bureau in advance, including the type, style, use, working pressure, installation location, and its relationship to other workplaces, for review and approval before starting work. Those who have already installed boilers must also submit plans and drawings to the Bureau for review. Article 4: When a mechanical engineer conducts an inspection, a factory inspector from the Bureau must be present. Article 5: When a mechanical engineer deems the inspection to be satisfactory, they should issue a certificate of inspection and send a copy of the certificate to the Bureau for record. The form of the aforementioned certificate of inspection will be determined separately. Article 6: The certificate of inspection of the boiler should state the following items: (1) The name of the mechanical engineer and the location of their office. (2) The date of inspection and its validity period. (3) The maximum pressure that the boiler can withstand during normal operation. (4) The number, age, structure, and manufacturer's name of the boiler. (5) Other matters concerning the installation, use, and management of the boiler. Article 7: The validity period of the certificate of inspection of the boiler depends on the material, structure, and usage of the boiler, but should not exceed one year at most. Article 8: For any boiler that fails the inspection, the mechanical engineer should prohibit its use and report the inspection situation to the Bureau. After the factory repairs it according to the mechanical engineer's instructions and passes the re-inspection, a certificate of inspection will be issued. Article 9: If a boiler is damaged, experiences abnormalities, or is mismanaged during the validity period of the certificate of inspection, resulting in safety hazards, the Bureau may suspend its use or revoke its certificate at any time. Article 10: The detailed standards for boiler inspection will be determined separately. Article 11: These measures will be implemented from the date of approval and announcement by the Municipal Government.

Agricultural Loan Syndicate Regulations: Measures for Cotton Transport and Sales Loans

The New Voice News Agency reports that the China Agricultural Loan Syndicate has allocated 1.4 million yuan to handle cotton transport and sales loans for Shaanxi, Shanxi, Hebei, and other three provinces in the Republic of China in 1936. The current loan measures are handled in accordance with the measures set by the cotton production improvement office of the Central Cotton Production Improvement Institute. The measures are recorded as follows: "Because cooperatives lack funds themselves, the initial working capital required for the cotton that is pre-paid at 70% of the flower price, i.e., the cotton that is cooperatively transported and sold, and the cotton that is purchased from members with full payment, averages 4,000 yuan per cooperative, totaling approximately 60,000 yuan. Borrow from the syndicate with the average share capital of each cooperative, approximately 1,000 yuan, deposited in the syndicate as collateral for losses. The flower payment should be made according to the prescribed standards, and the improvement institute is responsible for and supervises the handling. The aforementioned borrowed working capital must be deducted in full when the business is nearing completion, and it is estimated that the price obtained from the sale of cotton from each cooperative is sufficient to repay the principal and interest of the loan, in order to prepare for returning it to the syndicate. At the same time, the instructors of each cooperative must report the number of flowers nearing the end of the season in their respective locations, so that the branch offices can be prepared for the aforementioned calculation."

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Requests Ministry of Finance to Levy Tax on Privately Refined Kerosene

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a memorial to the Ministry of Finance yesterday, requesting action on the matter. On the 10th of this month, the Petroleum Industry Association sent a letter stating that since the import tax on kerosene has been increased several times, it has reached 4.6 yuan per pair (i.e., ten gallons) in national currency. Cunning merchants in various places are competing to refine kerosene from diesel to avoid heavy taxes. This has been going on for several years. In order to prevent tax evasion, the customs has revised the diesel tax regulations to remedy the situation and clearly stipulated that any oil refinery must be approved by the local officials and reported to the customs for approval and assignment of personnel to monitor and collect taxes. The legislation to protect legitimate merchants and prevent tax evasion is very thorough. Unexpectedly, since last year, the number of oil refineries has been increasing, all refining with low-grade diesel, cleverly evading customs duties as before. The products are flooding the market, prices have plummeted, and the losses of all imported kerosene are countless. The government's treatment of oil merchants must be equal, and kerosene and diesel are not domestically produced. If clever tax evasion is allowed to continue, how can the national treasury be valued and fairness be shown? For the sake of the present, the Ministry should forward the matter to the Ministry of Finance to exempt all of the heavy import tax on kerosene, so that cunning people will have no means to use their skills, and the burden can be reduced in today's collapsed rural economy. If it is difficult to implement due to public debt funds, the Ministry should also consult with the provincial and municipal governments to order the police to strictly investigate privately established refineries and order them to report to the government for approval in accordance with the customs regulations, and assign personnel to monitor and collect taxes, similar to the cigarette factory method, which will surely increase annual revenue. If none of the above measures are adopted, imported oil merchants will be in imminent danger and will have to change their industries and engage in oil refining, which will completely eliminate the customs duties of more than 50 million yuan. The association serves the people and is heartbroken that domestic kerosene has not yet been exploited, and the sale of foreign goods is painful. However, the amount of regular tax paid over the years is more than millions, and they have never complained about serving the country. However, with the rampant private oil and the government indifferent, business is declining and bankruptcy is imminent. They have to make a sincere statement. They dare to ask the Chamber to forward the matter to the Ministry of Finance and promptly take strict measures to punish evasion and show fairness. The committee is awaiting orders. After investigating, the establishment of factories by Chinese to refine kerosene from diesel is also a strategy of changing semi-finished products into refined products and reducing leakage. However, once the import tax on diesel is paid, it can be refined without paying any more taxes. The difference between tax-exempt and taxable kerosene is too great. Since there is a door for evasion, it does not seem fair. The association requests that the factories that refine kerosene from diesel be subject to a balanced tax rate, similar to the cigarette factories, and a unified tax be collected, so that manufacturers can still make a profit, and the national tax revenue and the oil merchants' business can be preserved. It seems to be a well-considered and comprehensive strategy, and it is reasonable to request the Ministry to review and approve it for implementation. It is convenient for the public.

Du Yuesheng of the Gaoqiao Rural Improvement Association Requests Repair of Ponds; Seawater Will Connect with Fields; Prevention of Mid-Autumn Tide Disaster is Necessary

The Gaoqiao seawall in Pudong, this city, is extremely thin, and after being violently impacted by the strong wind and rain on the 3rd of this month, several places suddenly collapsed, and the situation is extremely serious.
