The original letter is recorded below. Respected Sirs: The Pudong seawall extends for more than twenty li from the mouth of the Wusong River to the Daijiazhai section, protecting millions of people in our Pudong area. However, the water is rapid and the seawall is thin, impacting each other, and there is always concern about collapse. The devastating events of 1933 still frighten the people. Who would have known that since the beginning of autumn, the sea level has risen and hurricanes have occurred repeatedly. From the Jiazhai section of the Gaoqiao District ShuiTian Huangjiazhai seawall, which is three miles long, it is felt that it is not safe from one morning to the next, and the situation is extremely dangerous. After the storm tide on the 3rd of this month, the seawall was further shaken. The Longwang Temple at the Daijiazhai Seaside Bathing Beach and the four places in Jiazhai section of the Gaoqiao District ShuiTian Huangjiazhai have been washed into breaches, and the seawater outside the seawall will be connected to the fields inside the seawall. If it is struck by another storm tide, the flood will flow back and become a waterlogged country. What's more, the Mid-Autumn Festival tide is imminent. Alas, my people, worried that they will live with fish and turtles, are in great sorrow day and night, not knowing what to do. If we do not take measures to repair it as soon as possible, the great disaster is at hand. I have seen this and respectfully list the dangerous situation and respectfully ask your Bureau to investigate the facts and instruct the local authorities to quickly engage in dike construction and rescue to relieve the crisis and reassure the people. I hope you will approve and adopt it. The gratitude of the people is not only mine.

Full Text of the Du Chongyuan Case Verdict: Supreme Court Explains Reasons in Detail; Sentence Changed Regarding Confiscation

Following the two trials of Mr. Du Chongyuan, the person in charge of *New Life Weekly*, Mrs. Hou Yuzhi, Mr. Du's wife, disagreed and independently appealed. Lawyers Yu Zhong and Luo drafted the appeal. The Supreme Court has now issued its verdict. The full text is recorded below:

(Year 25, Shang Zi No. 832) Appellant Hou Yuzhi, female, wife of Du Chongyuan, age 29, resident of No. 52, Xinyu Lane, Meibai Road, Shanghai. Defendant Du Chongyuan, male, age 39, engaged in industry, resident of *New Life Weekly* office, Fuxing Lane, Sima Road, Shanghai. The above-named appellant filed an appeal against the first instance verdict issued by the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court on July 9th, Republic of China Year 24, in the case of the defendant's offense against international relations. This court's verdict is as follows:

Main Text

The portion of the original verdict concerning the conviction and sentence is revoked. Du Chongyuan is sentenced to imprisonment for one year and two months for disseminating writings and jointly defaming the head of a friendly nation.

Reasons

The appellant's appeal raises approximately three points, namely: (1) Whether the appeal should be accepted; (2) Whether the conditions for prosecution are met; (3) Whether criminal liability exists. Regarding the first point, the issue of appeal has already been decided by this court on September 11th of last year, with a ruling to accept the appeal, so further explanation is unnecessary. As for the second point, it states that Article 119 of the Criminal Code stipulates that offenses against reputation under Article 116 and offenses under Article 118 require a request from the foreign government for prosecution. The method of making such a request is also clearly stipulated in Article 220, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Procedure Law (which is a mistake; it should be Article 222, Paragraph 1). Now, upon examining the facts stated in the original verdict and the original indictment, this case was initiated solely by a request from the Japanese Consul-General in Shanghai to the Shanghai Municipal Government, which then ordered the Public Security Bureau to forward the investigation and prosecution. Since the Consul-General in Shanghai cannot be considered the representative of the foreign government, and the Shanghai Municipal Government and the Public Security Bureau cannot consider themselves the Ministry of Foreign Affairs or the highest judicial administrative authority, both the requester and the recipient of the request are unqualified. Therefore, the request cannot be considered legal, and the conditions for prosecution are still lacking. The prosecutor's indictment based on this is an improper acceptance of the case. The third point states that *New Life Weekly*, Volume 2, Issue 15, was published on May 4th of this year (Year 24), while Du Chongyuan was staying in Jiangxi before that date. The letter from the Jiangxi Pottery Management Bureau has been presented as evidence, sufficient to prove that Du Chongyuan did not participate in or know about the publication and distribution of "Gossip Emperor." The original trial did not investigate in detail whether the author "Yishui," who signed the article, was another person, or whether the manuscript had actually been reviewed by Du Chongyuan. Instead, it simply considered that Du Chongyuan, as the editor and publisher, was legally responsible, which shows a lack of thoroughness in the trial. Furthermore, since the author of "Gossip Emperor," Yishui, is someone else, the original intention of the author, whether it contained defamatory intent, could not be speculated by Du Chongyuan, who was unaware. However, if the allegedly defamatory statement is supported by substantial evidence based on objective facts, sufficient to show that it is not entirely without basis, and does not involve private morality, Article 310, Paragraph 3 of the Criminal Code still provides an explicit exemption from punishment. In monarchical states, the ideology of the emperor's position varies significantly with the era and culture, with major differences in the so-called divine right theory, patriarchal theory, property theory, and state organ theory. In Japan, since the Meiji and Taisho eras, constitutional scholars in that country have centered their discussions on the organ theory and the subject theory. Therefore, the description of the Japanese Emperor in "Gossip Emperor" has a basis in academic theory and cannot be regarded as a defamatory intention. Moreover, "Gossip Emperor" does not exclusively target the monarch of Japan for gossip. It does not contain a factual infringement on the Japanese Emperor's personality, and at most, it only states that the Emperor's authority is gradually declining. Since it does not harm the general reputation of being an emperor, it is unlikely to harm the Japanese Emperor's personality. It is therefore difficult to say that the author has legally fulfilled the general requirements for the crime of defamation. In addition to the improper distinction regarding the existence of criminal liability, the application of the sentencing provisions cannot be said to be free of error. This court believes that the crime of defamation under Article 310, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Code is committed merely by disseminating writings or drawings to point out or spread facts sufficient to damage the reputation of others. It does not require that the reputation of the person being defamed actually be damaged as a necessary element. As for whether those facts are sufficient to damage reputation, it is naturally interpreted that the position of the person being defamed should be concretely observed, and the standard of judgment cannot be based on general abstract views. (The provisions of Article 325, Paragraph 2 of the old Criminal Code are the same.) After examining *New Life Weekly*, Volume 2, Issue 15, submitted by the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, the article "Gossip Emperor," signed by Yishui, states: "As far as we know, the Emperor of Japan is a biologist. He has to be the Emperor because of hereditary succession. Everything is done in the name of the Emperor, but in fact, he has no say. The Emperor is used when receiving foreign guests, when reviewing troops, and when holding grand ceremonies. Otherwise, the Emperor is forgotten by the people. The Japanese military and the bourgeoisie are the true rulers of Japan... At present, Japan is reluctant to abandon this antique called the Emperor, which is of great help to the current stage of Japanese rule. It tries to use the Emperor to ease the conflicts between all internal classes and to cover up the crimes of some people... Japan elevates the Emperor to be inviolable, but in fact, he is also a puppet of the modern true rulers." These words not only contain insulting language towards the head of a friendly nation but also point out facts sufficient to damage the dignity of his position. It is in line with the constituent elements of the crime of defamation. The appellant's argument that the essay does not exclusively target the monarch of Japan and does not contain any factual infringement on the Emperor's personality and does not constitute defamation is an abnormal view. Although the appellant also submitted writings by Japanese constitutional scholars, stating that there are still debates among scholars in that country regarding the Emperor's constitutional position, and that the content of the essay is not entirely without basis, claiming that it meets the exemption conditions of Article 310, Paragraph 3 of the Criminal Code, it is not known that the provision is only exempt from punishment if the defamed matter can be proven to be true. The writings of Japanese scholars submitted by the appellant are purely academic discussions and are not related to the content of the preceding essay. They cannot prove that the matters pointed out in the original text are true. How can they be used as an argument for exemption? As the defendant served as the editor and publisher of *New Life Weekly*, he should be responsible for the content of the publication. The defendant himself confessed this during the investigation. Although the article "Gossip Emperor" was published under the name of Yishui, the defendant implemented its publication. Unless there is conclusive proof that he was unaware, he cannot shirk joint responsibility. Although the defendant argued that he was still staying in Jiangxi when the weekly was published and did not participate in Shanghai, he presented a letter from the Jiangxi Pottery Administration sent to his friend Sun Xuxian in Shanghai as evidence. However, it is not necessary for the editor to be present at the place of publication in order to review the text published in the publication. Even if the defendant was not in Shanghai when the publication was published, it is still not enough to refute the accusations against him. The original trial found the defendant responsible for the joint crime of harming the reputation of the head of a friendly nation, and taking into account the impact of the crime, sentenced him to imprisonment for one year and two months, which is legally sound. The appellant's allegations on this point are also clearly untenable. Furthermore, Article 119 of the Criminal Code states that the crime of harming reputation under Article 116 requires a request from the foreign government for prosecution (the provisions of Article 127 of the old Criminal Code are the same). The so-called "request by the foreign government" is not limited to a direct request by the foreign government; it also has the effect of a legal request when the foreign government authorizes its subordinate officials to do so. Furthermore, according to Article 222, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Procedure Law, this request must be made through the Minister of Foreign Affairs consulting the highest judicial administrative authority, and the relevant prosecutor must be notified. However, this is not a required procedure for making the request. Therefore, even if the foreign government's request does not go through the procedures outlined in that article, as long as the expression of the request has reached the relevant prosecutor, it should be considered legal. According to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau's official letter to the prosecutor of the original court in this case, it only stated "Upon receiving a telegram from the Municipal Government stating that the Japanese Consul-General came to the office to request prosecution in accordance with the law." It is unclear whether the Japanese Consul-General in Shanghai was ordered by the government to act on its behalf. However, the Third Instance Court may investigate the facts in accordance with Article 386 of the Criminal Procedure Law regarding whether the original trial accepted the lawsuit. This court has obtained an official letter from the Shanghai Municipal Government to the prosecutor of the original court, which vaguely states, "In this case, the Japanese Consul-General was ordered by his government to personally come to the office to request legal action." It is beyond doubt that he was ordered to act on his behalf. The expression of this request has also reached the relevant prosecutor, and the conditions for prosecution are complete. The original trial's acceptance of the lawsuit was not improper. The appellant's accusation that the request was made by the Japanese Consul-General in Shanghai to the Shanghai Municipal Government, which ordered the Public Security Bureau to forward the investigation, is a misunderstanding. However, Article 2, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Code states, "If the law changes after the act, the law in force at the time of the judgment shall apply. However, if the law in force before the judgment is more beneficial to the actor, the most beneficial law to the actor shall apply." This refers to comparing the laws in force before the judgment as a whole and applying the one that is most beneficial to the actor. It is not possible to selectively apply the beneficial parts. The defendant committed the crime before the Criminal Code came into effect. According to the law in force before the judgment, he committed the crimes under Articles 42, 122, and 325, Paragraph 2 of the old Criminal Code. The most severe principal penalty under that article is imprisonment for one year or less. After increasing it by one-third, it is imprisonment for one year and four months. Comparing it with the penalty at the time of the judgment, that is, the penalty under Articles 28, 116, and 310, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Code, the old Criminal Code is lighter. It is legal to apply the old law as a whole for sentencing. The original verdict only applied the provisions of Article 325, Paragraph 2 of the old Criminal Code for the principal penalty for the crime of defamation. The remaining legal provisions still followed the new law, which is a mistake. Furthermore, only items belonging to the offender and used for the commission of the crime can be confiscated. Article 38, Paragraph 3 of the Criminal Code and the latter part of Article 62, Paragraph 1 of the old Criminal Code clearly stipulate this. *New Life Weekly*, Volume 2, Issue 15, on file, was transferred by the Shanghai Municipal Government for reference and does not belong to the offender. It is not eligible for confiscation under the law. The original verdict wrongly treated the publication as being used for the commission of the crime and confiscated it. This is not legal and should be revoked and changed by this court in order to correct the error. The appeal is not entirely without merit. The number of days of detention before the judgment is final that are used to offset the term of imprisonment is a matter of execution. According to the precedent of this court, the new law should be applied. According to Article 46 of the Criminal Code, one day should naturally offset one day of imprisonment, without the need to further advise in the main text.

Based on the above conclusion, in accordance with Articles 389 and 390, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Procedure Law, Article 2, Paragraph 1 (but not the provision) of the Criminal Code, and Articles 42, 122, 325 Paragraph 2 and 127 of the old Criminal Code, the judgment is as stated in the main text. August 26, Republic of China Year 25, Ninth Criminal Division of the Supreme Court. Presiding Judge Zhang Xiaolin; Judges Sun Lu, Xu Zaofeng, Ouyang Xu, Sun Yuan. This is certified as a true copy of the original. Clerk Long Puji. August 29, Republic of China Year 25.

Bandit Wang Er Refuses Arrest, Killed by Bullet Wound

Ni Fusheng and Wang Er, both from Jiangbei, sneaked into the entrance of Hongan Lane on Bazilu around 1:00 PM the day before yesterday, holding a wooden fake pistol, planning to rob a Guangdong woman, Du Renyi, of her purse, which contained five yuan in banknotes. They fled to the intersection of Bazilu and Sichuan Road, where Chinese Inspector Zhang Desheng and Feng Chen of the Hongkou Police Station and Chinese Constable No. 1890 arrived after hearing the alarm. Seeing Wang Er holding a pistol and resisting arrest, Chinese Constable No. 1890 fired his gun and knocked him down to arrest him. It was only then that it was known that his pistol was a fake. Ni Fusheng was also subsequently captured and taken to the police station. After questioning, it was learned that Wang Er (also known as Chen Zhengfa) was 32 years old and had previously been sentenced to 15 years for committing a crime. He died at 6:00 AM the next morning due to a wound to a vital part. The body was taken to the forensic examination office on Feilun Road. Bandit Ni was escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Lawyer Zhang Shizhu of the Public Works Department explained the case and requested a postponement. Then, the detectives reported the process of arresting the two thieves and presented a fake pistol for inspection. Du Renyi, Xu Yishan, and Tian Baochang also described the situation of being robbed and chased. When Ni Fusheng was questioned, his confession was evasive. Judge Zhong Qing ordered him to be returned to custody and rescheduled the hearing. Tang, a prosecutor from the court, went to the Wang Er's office and determined that Wang Er, the deceased, had been shot to death by Chinese Constable No. 1890 for robbery and resisting arrest. There was no family to claim the body, so the body was handed over to Pushan Villa for collection. Co-offender Ni Fusheng has also been prosecuted by the police station.

Detailed Account of the Discovery of Two Nude Corpses, Male and Female, at a Hongkou Women's Hospital; Female Suspect Liang Meiyu Fled Before Arrest; Corpses' Faces Unrecognizable, Apparently Strangled; Female Servant Fei Wangshi Temporarily Detained for Testimony

The Hongkou Women's Hospital, located at 290 Zhaofeng Road, Hongkou, was rented by Liang Meiyu, a female doctor and concubine of a Mr. Liang, from the Christian Jubilee Church last year. Besides Mr. Liang and Liang Meiyu living together, Mr. Liang's first wife, Meiyu's younger sister, and Fei Wangshi, a female servant from Wuxi, all lived upstairs in the hospital. On the 7th of this month, the Liangs suddenly moved all their valuables away, leaving only a few items in the rooms and leaving a substitute female servant of Fei Wangshi to guard the place. Until the other day, a deacon of the Jubilee Church suddenly noticed an unusually strong foul odor emanating from the hospital's examination room, which aroused his suspicion. He then ordered the female servant on guard to find the source of the odor, but because the room was tightly sealed, she could not enter. Looking through the window, she found nothing. Thus, at 6:00 p.m. the day before, she reported to the Huishan Police Station, which ordered Chinese detectives Huang Fugen and Cui Chengke, along with Western detectives and firefighters, to rush to the scene. They opened the door to the room and found a large, newly nailed rectangular tin box, with traces of lime nearby. The foul odor came from this box. They pried open the floorboards, and to their horror, discovered two nude corpses underneath, both covered with lime, their backs facing up.

They had already begun to decompose, and their faces were difficult to recognize, but it was roughly determined that one was male and one was female, though this could not be confirmed. At this time, Fei Wangshi also arrived at the scene, and the detectives immediately detained her. They then sent the corpses by hearse to the forensic examination office on Feilun Road. According to Fei Wangshi, she had been employed at the hospital since December of last year. On the 1st of this month, she returned to Wuxi and came back to Shanghai at 5:30 p.m. the day before. The female doctor Liang Meiyu's husband was sometimes called Mr. Liang and sometimes Mr. Wang. It was also known that he had another clinic located at No. 1, Lane 353, Nanjing Road, room 315 of the

Dalu Bazaar. The detectives then rushed to investigate, but found that the location was the clinic of Dr. Hou Guangdi, and there was no one inside. Later, checking the telephone directory, they found that Hou lived at 292 Binlang Road, so they rushed there again, but the house was already empty and had been vacated. They then discovered that Hou had opened a hospital at 370 Minguo Road a month ago, and went to investigate, but found no one there either. Subsequently, the detectives learned that Liang Meiyu was hiding at her sister's house at No. 10 Yile Lane, Tangshan Road.

They immediately went to arrest her, but Liang had left moments before. However, according to Fei Wangshi, before she returned to Wuxi, a woman with a serious illness came to the clinic for consultation. The doctor told her to stay at the hospital for treatment, and the woman's husband also stayed at the hospital. According to Yang Youmei, the gatekeeper of the hospital, on the 4th of this month, he heard the sound of floorboards being pried up in the hospital, but he did not pay attention at the time. Yesterday morning, the police sent Fei Wangshi to the Third Criminal Court of the Special No. 1 Court. Zhang Shizhu, the police lawyer, explained the situation in detail and requested that she be detained for further investigation. A deacon of the Jubilee Church then testified about the

circumstances of the discovery. When questioned, Fei Wangshi claimed that she knew nothing about the matter and that she had only arrived in Shanghai at 5:30 p.m. yesterday. Judge Zhong Qing reviewed the statement and ordered that Fei Wangshi be detained until the 18th of this month for further questioning. Subsequently, Tang, the prosecutor of the Special No. 1 Court, summoned Wei Ligong and Zhang Yan, two forensic doctors, and Wang Zuyi, a court clerk, to the forensic examination office to examine the bodies. He then ordered Fei Wangshi to go to the morgue to identify the two corpses. Because their faces had decomposed, they could not be identified. According to the forensic examination, it was determined that the two corpses were

one male and one female. The male's neck still had rope and gauze wrapped around it, while the female's neck had no rope, only gauze. Both corpses were about thirty years old, and their time of death was about one or two weeks ago. The forensic doctors then dissected the female corpse and found gauze adhering to her genital area. According to the forensic doctors' observations, it was either due to an abortion or a miscarriage, but it was still difficult to determine. However, it could be determined that she had been strangled. The gauze from the genital area was taken back by the forensic doctors for further study. Prosecutor Tang ordered that the deaths of the unnamed man and unnamed woman were determined to be due to strangulation. Before the identity of the corpses can be determined, the corpses will be handed over to the Pushan Villa for collection. The criminal in this case should be thoroughly investigated by the relevant police station and brought to justice.

Zhao Fengxiang Sentenced to Twelve Years for Selling Morphine

Zhao Fengxiang was arrested by the French police on November 22 last year for illegally selling the drug morphine. Several packages of morphine were found on his person. He was sent to the Special No. 2 Court and sentenced to imprisonment. During the interrogation, Zhao confessed that he was instructed by Cai Tingliang, his boss, to sell the drugs, and the court issued an arrest warrant to the police station to arrest Cai Tingliang. Until recently, detectives Zhou Bingxuan and Ma Yizhi arrested Cai Tingliang (nicknamed "Long-legged Ahui," 30, from Suzhou) and found 26 packages of morphine in a hidden tin bucket in his home. He was sent to the Special No. 2 Court and prosecuted according to law. All details have been recorded in the newspaper. Judge Zhang Chaozuo has concluded the interrogation, and at 10:00 a.m. yesterday, Judge Zhang presided over the First Criminal Court and sentenced Cai Tingliang to thirteen years of imprisonment for selling opium substitutes and deprived him of his civil rights for ten years. The 26 packages of morphine were confiscated and destroyed.

Chen Huizhang's Tragic Death: Coercion and Reconciliation Case Concluded, Englishman Massey Testifies in Court, Sentencing Scheduled for the 17th of This Month

Chen Huizhang, a rickshaw puller, was beaten to death by British sailors in front of the British General Association on July 8 of this year. The All Circles organized a support association for the tragic death case, which caused a great sensation. Unexpectedly, it was later reconciled for a price of six hundred yuan. After the reconciliation, the father Chen Xizhu and wife Chen Zang sued Xu Jiesheng, a cadre of the Ximen Branch of the Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Association, Zhang Dengying, the general manager of the Mutual Aid Association, and Miao Jiande, for colluding with Cao Ada and impersonating Chen Zang's brother. Entrusted by Massey, the Englishman who was the chairman of the Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Association and the director of the Bureau of Public Works, they coerced her to put her fingerprints on the document to reconcile the death for six hundred yuan, and two hundred yuan was deducted, so she only received four hundred yuan. The deceased died unjustly, and the living suffered. They were distraught, flattering foreigners, and requested an investigation. After being summoned, the defendants claimed that they were acting with sincerity, seeking justice for the deceased and helping the living. They did not defraud or oppress them. The lady received the compensation from the police station herself, and they did not deduct any money. There was a background to harm them. They asked for Massey to be summoned to testify. Yesterday morning, Zhang Peiming, a judge of the District Court, opened the court and continued to examine the witness. Massey said that he was 60 years old, British, and was the director of motor vehicle affairs in the Bureau of Public Works, residing at No. 179 Jessfield Road. He asked if on July 8 of this year, a rickshaw puller was beaten to death by British sailors, and if you handled the matter of giving six hundred yuan. He answered, the reconciliation was handled by his wife. He asked, according to Xu Jiesheng, was the six hundred yuan paid at your place. He answered, his wife came to my office and said that she had received it. He asked, how much money did she get. He answered, six hundred yuan. He asked, did this six hundred yuan pass through your office. He answered, the woman received a total of six hundred yuan, which was given to her by the police station. She said that she was afraid of danger, so she put five hundred yuan in my office, and she took away one hundred yuan. He asked, when did she take the remaining five hundred yuan. He answered, she came to take it the next day. He asked, did the police station give her this money. The answer is that a person surnamed Yang in the police station represented the British sailor to pay her. He asked, how many people went to the police station in total. He answered, he did not see the woman directly, his subordinates reported it to me. He asked, since this woman got the money, why did she report to you. He answered, because I am the chairman of the Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Association, and she came to thank me. He asked, which of them went to the police station. He answered, his wife, her brother, and Xu Jiesheng. He asked, did Zhang Dengying go. He answered, no. He asked, who asked you to take care of this matter. He answered, Xu Jielian called me. At this point, Massey presented a written statement, claiming that this was the whole story and that there was a background of trouble now, requesting the court to accept the testimony. At this point, the official life began to debate. After the lawyers for both parties argued vigorously, the questioner announced the end of the debate and scheduled the sentencing for the 17th of this month.

The Hardships of Slum Dwellers: The Municipal Federation Pleads on Their Behalf

According to Xin Sheng She, the Shanghai First Special District Citizens' Federation sent a letter to the Bureau of Public Works of the Public Concession yesterday, stating: "To whom it may concern, it is noted that the Shanghai Slum Dwellers' Federation has sent a letter stating that slum dwellers are the poorest citizens living in Shanghai. They are unable to rent houses, so they hastily build sheds in a corner of Pudong, barely sheltering from the wind and rain, in the hope of eking out a living and working hard. The Bureau of Public Works of the Public Concession has ordered them to demolish their homes by a deadline, disregarding our working-class compatriots. If this is implemented, they will be displaced and suffer even more. Who can not feel sympathy for this situation? We have appealed to all sectors of society in this city to rise up and provide assistance. At the same time, our Federation sent a letter to the Bureau of Public Works on August 31, requesting five conditions: (1) In the future, our slum dwellers will automatically restrict themselves from increasing in number; (2) If the landlord builds houses or the Bureau of Public Works needs to open roads, the slum dwellers will move; (3) Comply with the guidance of the Municipal Bureau of Wealth and improve sanitation facilities; (4) Request the Bureau of Public Works to revoke the demolition order to ensure their livelihood; (5) Request the Bureau of Public Works to promptly allocate funds to build public housing to accommodate slum dwellers in order to eliminate them in stages. While this case is being negotiated and the Bureau of Public Works has not made a clear statement, on September 2, the Yangshupu Police Station led a large number of Chinese and Western detectives and more than 80 workers, riding in police vehicles, and forcibly demolished the sheds at No. 448 Chaoyang Road, regardless of the circumstances. They beat people, causing more than 40 slum dwellers to be injured, and arrested and transferred them to the court, charging them with Article 150 of the Criminal Law. As a result, all the slum dwellers panicked and convened a meeting to make five resolutions: (1) Request the Bureau of Public Works to stop the demolition; (2) Detectives who are derelict in their duties should be punished; (3) Guarantee that the same situation will not happen again in the future; (4) Release the arrested poor people; (5) The Bureau of Public Works shall be responsible for medical expenses and compensation for losses for the injured. The records are on file. We have often sent letters to the Bureau of Public Works requesting implementation. However, due to the anxiety and uneasiness of the people, we dare to ask your Federation to consider the hardships of the small and weak ethnic groups and approve the above five conditions to negotiate with the Bureau of Public Works again, so that they can be fully implemented, and our tens of thousands of slum dwellers will benefit greatly. The Federation has checked that slum dwellers are the poorest of the poor in the city. The Federation deeply regrets the unfortunate case of Chaoyang Road. It should be considered that the slums are suffering and should be decided to be implemented as requested."

In the case of the robbery of cash worth more than one thousand yuan at Xue Mai Luo Accounting Firm, Wanhao, Edward Road, French Concession, in the afternoon of June 9, 1934, the suspect Zhang Zuming (Ningbo native, shareholder of Ruichangshun No. 5 Yu, Broadway Road) was arrested after reporting to the police station. Because there was no evidence of a crime, Zhang, Zhuang, Wang, and Tang were declared innocent. Because the Police Department repeatedly appealed, the

third trial still upheld the original judgment. Later, Zhang Zuming hired a lawyer to send a letter to Zhou Jinggeng (victim of the robbery), a comprador at Xue Mai Luo Accounting Firm, accusing him of being innocently implicated in the detention and suffering losses, and demanding compensation of 32,000 yuan. Because Zhou ignored it, Zhang filed a complaint with the Criminal Court of the Special Court, suing Zhou Jinggeng, Gao Yuhua, Feng Ti'e, Wan Guirong, Qian Genghua, Wang Guixiang, and others for jointly fabricating evidence and falsely accusing him, requesting an investigation, and attached a civil suit, seeking

damages of 50,000 yuan. At the same time, Zhuang Jimeng also felt unwilling to be unjustly accused by Zhang Zuming, detained, and imprisoned, so he hired a lawyer to file a complaint with the Criminal Court of the Special No. 1 Court, suing Zhang Zuming for the crime of false accusation, and attached a civil suit, seeking damages of 50,000 yuan. After the trial by the Special No. 1 Court, the case was transferred to the Special No. 2 Court for trial due to incorrect jurisdiction in the French Concession. The Special No. 2 Court filed the complaint, and the case was handled by the former Judge Li Changnian.

He said that he accused the defendants Zhou Jinggeng et al. of false testimony and false accusation. At that time, I was walking properly and was identified as a robber, detained by the police station, and beaten, causing damage to my reputation, spirit, and business.

Various damages were requested for investigation and judgment, and compensation was ordered for my losses of 30,000 yuan. Zhou Jinggeng testified that I was not at the scene during the robbery. After the robbery, I reported to the police station. When the robber searched Gao Yushu, he said that he had copied morphine. Please ask Gao about a package of banknotes robbed from Gao's side. After the police station detained the plaintiff, I only submitted a complaint and filed a private lawsuit, and did not name and report the plaintiff as a thief. Gao Yushu testified that he clearly saw the face of the robber who robbed me. It was absolutely impossible to make a mistake. After the police station arrested the plaintiff, he called me to identify him in the crowd. If it wasn't him, he said

How could he have confessed so clearly when his mind was confused? He was the first to enter the door with a pistol. I was robbed of 6,000 yuan. Feng Ti'e testified that the police station called me to identify him. I identified the plaintiff in the crowd because the plaintiff was the first person to enter the door during the robbery. The remaining Wan Guirong, Qian Genghua, Wang Guixiang, etc. had the same testimony. At this point, the official told that the circumstances of the case were all in the file, and today the debate can be opened. Then the plaintiff's agent lawyer Lu Dingkui and the defendant's defense lawyers Bian Jialu and Zhang Shanle

debated fiercely. The plaintiff's lawyer said that the defendants' identification of the plaintiff as a thief was recorded in detail in the public prosecution record and should be judged according to law. The defendant's defense lawyer said that the plaintiff's allegations were all unsubstantiated and requested that the defendant be declared innocent. After the debate, the court announced the end of the debate and scheduled the sentencing for 2:00 p.m. on the 15th. Then Zhuang Jimeng sued Zhang Zuming for false accusation. The plaintiff Zhuang Jimeng said that the defendant Zhang Zuming was first arrested and falsely accused me, Wang Lianyou, and Tang Qingyue, and was also arrested and sent to your court

The judgment was innocent. At that time, Zhang confessed in the police station that I had used all my pistols to rob. Because I often patrolled specially, I had a pistol, and he also confessed that the stolen money was divided in my car after the robbery. There was no basis at all. I requested an investigation. After I was arrested, my reputation, body, and business were all damaged. I attached a civil suit, seeking compensation for losses of 50,000 yuan. Asked the defendant Zhang Zuming, at that time I was arrested to the police station, asked me to confess my accomplices, slapped me in the face, and took a wooden stick to hit me, and said that if I didn't tell, I would grind electricity. I was forced to lose consciousness and could not confess the plaintiff, etc. However, the plaintiff and I were classmates and relatives. Xue Shuncai, Suspected of Killing Shi, Is Innocent: The Deceased's Organs Are Transported to Shanghai, Forensic Examination Shows No Poison

Xue Shunxiang, 23, a Yangzhou native and owner of the Qingji Barber Shop at No. 155 Duck Road, lived with his mother, Xie, and brothers Shuncai and Shunxi. On December 4th of last year, Xie took her young son Shunxi back to her hometown for marriage. Shunxiang suddenly suffered from a foot disease, was bedridden and unable to move. On the evening of the 8th, he was thirsty and asked his younger brother Shuncai to fetch him tea to quench his thirst. After closing his eyes and falling asleep, he passed away the next morning. His wife, Xia, reported the situation to the Jiaxing Road Police Station, which sent detectives to arrest Xue Shuncai and send him to the First Special District Court. The first instance sentenced him to life imprisonment. Xue Shuncai refused to accept the verdict and appealed to the Second Branch Court of the High Court. The High Court then sent a document to the Jiangdu local court, ordering the dissection of Xue Shunxiang's body, the removal of his organs, which were placed in a glass bottle and transported to Shanghai, and handed over to forensic doctor Zhen Ru for detailed examination. The result showed no poison. After deliberation and conclusion, the judgment was to be announced. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Yu Hua and two judges, Nie and Xiao, presided over the court and ruled that Xue Shuncai's original sentence was revoked and he was declared innocent. The police lawyer Jingxian requested bail during the appeal period. Xue was returned to custody without bail.

Chinese Police Officer Sentenced to Death on Appeal for Manslaughter in Adultery Case: Killer Requests a Meeting with His Paramour, Judge Considers Denying Permission

Zhang Junmou, a Chinese police officer with badge number 2650 from the Huishan Police Station and a native of Anhui province, committed adultery with Wu Chenshi, the wife of Wu Yujing, a driver for the Xiang Sheng Automobile Company. Wu, along with his tenant Jiao Changgui and his wife, reported Zhang to the police. Harboring resentment, Zhang, accompanied by Wu Chenshi, went to No. , Tonghe Lane, Fuxu Road at approximately 5:00 AM on June 2nd of this year, fatally shot Jiao Changgui, and wounded Jiao's wife, Gu. Zhang Junmou and Wu Chenshi were apprehended on the spot and sent to the First Special Court for questioning. Zhang Junmou was found guilty of joint homicide and sentenced to death, while Wu Chenshi was sentenced to ten years of imprisonment. Zhang Junmou appealed the verdict to the Second Branch of the Higher Court. The appellate court concluded its review and, yesterday afternoon, Judge Yu Hua, along with judges Xiao and Nie, announced the judgment, dismissing the appeal and upholding the death sentence. Upon hearing the verdict, Zhang Junmou immediately requested a final meeting with Wu Chenshi. The court stated that Wu Chenshi had not submitted a request for such a meeting and that there was no explicit legal provision for it, therefore, the request was denied. However, the court informed Zhang that if he did not accept the verdict, he could appeal to the Supreme Court within ten days of receiving the written judgment.

Woman Missing: Bizarre Circumstances

Recently, strange cases have emerged one after another in this city. The case of the corpse in a suitcase found outside the Waibaidu Bridge on Suzhou Road in the Public Concession has just begun to show some clues, while the case of the two buried corpses at the Hongkou Women's Hospital has followed closely behind. Unexpectedly, a bizarre disappearance of a woman occurred in the French Concession yesterday. The strangeness and twists of the case surpass the previous two. The details are recorded below:

Brief Biography of the Sichuan Woman

Guo Yunxia, a Sichuan woman of thirty-some years old, is a woman who received a considerable education. She is inherently chivalrous and has a masculine spirit. She married a Mr. Zong, also from Sichuan. The couple came to Shanghai together and have been here for several years. Mr. Zong once served in the 19th Route Army. After the January 28th Incident ended, he returned to work for the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau but passed away in his Shanghai residence last spring due to poor health.

After Her Husband's Death

Mrs. Guo was distraught by her husband's death and nearly lost the will to live. Fortunately, a Mr. Wang, a close friend of Mr. Zong from Anhui, was in Shanghai. He stepped forward to handle all the funeral arrangements for Mr. Zong and raised funds for his coffin and burial. Mrs. Guo deeply appreciated Mr. Wang's kindness and wanted to repay him.

Running Around for a Friend

At the end of last month, Mr. Wang was suddenly arrested for a case and is currently detained in the Public Concession Police Station, awaiting a verdict. Upon hearing this news, Mrs. Guo, out of a sense of gratitude, began to run around and seek help from all sides for Mr. Wang. She even wrote to a businessman twice, requesting him to uphold justice.

Someone Visits

After Mrs. Guo sent the two letters, time passed without a response. Mrs. Guo gradually put the matter aside. Unexpectedly, at around 4:00 PM the day before yesterday, an uninvited guest, a man of around forty years old, with a sturdy build, a dark complexion, and wearing a grayish-brown silk shirt, arrived at Mrs. Guo's residence on the third floor of No. 2, Cishou Lane, Route Saopesai in the French Concession. He asked if Mrs. Wang was home.

Car Awaits

Mrs. Guo happened to be at home. She asked the visitor where he was from. The man said he was sent by Mr. So-and-so to invite her for a face-to-face conversation and urged her to go immediately, saying that a car was waiting at the entrance of the alley. As he spoke, the man handed Mrs. Guo his business card.

Reading the Card

Mrs. Guo took the card and read it carefully. On the front were the words "To Mrs. Wang, No. , Cishou Lane, Route Saopesai." On the back, it read, "Both letters have been received. Please come to discuss matters in person. Sincerely, Mrs. Wang." At the end was a signature, "Song," and a square seal, but upon closer inspection, the seal appeared to be hastily made.

Going by Car Together

After receiving the card, Mrs. Guo was overjoyed. She handed the card to her male servant, Gao Xisheng, immediately changed her clothes, and happily went with the visitor into a black sedan with a black license plate. As Mrs. Guo left, she specifically told the male servant, "I will be back soon. If anyone comes to visit, please ask them to wait."

Not Returning Late at Night

After Mrs. Guo left, Gao Xisheng, the male servant, stayed at the residence and waited. He waited until late at night but still did not see her return. At first, he suspected that Mrs. Guo had been delayed by important matters. Unexpectedly, by yesterday morning, Mrs. Guo still had not returned. He became suspicious and went to a nearby shop to call Mr. So-and-so's residence to inquire directly. He was told that Mr. So-and-so had not sent anyone with a card to invite Mrs. Guo for a conversation yesterday. Gao received this information and knew that something was wrong. He still hoped that Mrs. Guo would return safely, but all through last night, Mrs. Guo was still nowhere to be found.

The Lights on the Pujiang Buoys are Changed to Red: Notice from the Jianghai Customs Harbor Master: Effective October 1st

Harbor Master Te Baker of Jianghai Customs announced: It has been found that the buoys for mooring ships in the Pujiang River, with two buoys each, one above and one below, have each been equipped with a fixed white light when there are no ships moored. In order to make the routes between the buoys and the locations where ships turn around more clearly identifiable, it has been decided that, starting October 1st of this year, these white lights will be changed to red. The locations and numbers of all the buoys that should have the aforementioned red lights are listed in detail below: Upper Section (B) Buoys No. 12 and No. 6, Upper Section; (C) Salt Revenue Inspection Office Buoy and Buoy No. 1; First Section, China Merchants Bureau Jin Li Yuan Upper Buoy; Second Section, Jin Li Yuan Buoy; Second Section, Japanese Navy Buoy and British Navy Buoy; Third Section, Customs Transport Ship Buoy No. 1 and No. 3; Sixth Section, Buoy No. 1; Eighth Section, Buoy No. 10; Ninth Section, Buoy No. 11; Tenth Section, Buoys No. 17 and No. 17 (A); Eleventh Section, Buoy No. 30 (A); Lower Section, Buoys No. 31 and No. 44. All merchants are to be notified. This notice is hereby issued.

The Commodity Inspection Bureau Formulates Receipts for Raw Silk Pledges: Banking Association Sends Letters to All Banks for Verification

The Shanghai Banking Association has received a letter from the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry regarding the sample of raw silk pledge receipts. It is hereby forwarded to all member banks for verification. It begins, "To the point, we have received a letter from the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry stating, ‘Upon examination, silk merchants deposit raw silk in our bureau's silk warehouse and hold temporary receipts issued by our bureau's silk warehouse. Over time, they often use these receipts to borrow money from your industry to facilitate their turnover. For the sake of prudence, our bureau has specially printed a formal receipt for silk merchants to use when borrowing money. In addition to distributing them separately, we are sending the formal receipt sample for your verification and distribution to the industry for checking,' etc. We are forwarding this to all banks in the association and enclosing a sample for your verification and handling." Attached is a sample receipt with the following printed on it: "Receipt of the Silk Inspection Group, Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau, Ministry of Industry, National Government," with fields for date, number, consignor, silk type, number of pieces, brand, grade, package number, quantity, remarks, original receipt number, request number, and group leader, and stamped with the official seal. The right side of the receipt also notes, "(1) Raw silk stored in this bureau's silk warehouse has been insured against fire by this bureau. This bureau is responsible for losses covered by the fire insurance policy due to fire. However, this bureau is not responsible for losses due to other natural disasters or force majeure. (2) The raw silk stored in this bureau's silk warehouse, for which a receipt has been issued by this group, has been inspected and confirmed by this bureau to be the silk type listed in this receipt. The bureau is responsible for the contents."

The Case Against Le Zhenbao and Others is Concluded After Debate is Rescinded: Continued Interrogation Yesterday

The Shanghai West Paint Industry Association, represented by Ma Shangjie, filed a lawsuit in the Criminal Court of the Second Special Court through lawyers Zhang Shizhao and Chao Kun, against Le Zhenbao, Bei Runsheng, Zhang Lanping, Le Gengrong, and others regarding a property dispute with the Foreign Goods Business Association. The debate had originally concluded, and a date was set for the verdict. However, because the presiding judge felt that the case was not yet clear, he specifically rescinded the conclusion of the debate and ordered a new date for reopening the debate. This has been reported in previous issues. Yesterday, Judge Chen Shuoying summoned the plaintiff and members Wang Zuolin, Su Xiangxuan, Zhong Le Shan, Fang E, Dong Yuzhen, Li Shuyan, Hu Runsheng, Xia Kuisheng, Chen Gengsheng, Qin Lianliang, and others, as well as the defendants, to continue the hearing in the criminal court. The four defendants arrived with their defense attorneys, Yan Yinwu, Lin Rongqing, and Yuan Hanyun. The court first asked the plaintiff, Ma Shangjie, whether he had a letter of authorization from the association to represent them in the lawsuit. Ma replied that there were signatures from members and letters to prove that he had previously submitted them to the court and that the letter of authorization could be submitted tomorrow. The court then summoned the plaintiff's members, except for Shen Leshan, Ding Fang E, Li Shuyan, and Chen Gengsheng, who did not attend. Wang Zuolin, Su Xiangxuan, Dong Yuzhen, Hu Runsheng, Xia Kuisheng, Qin Lianliang, and the other six who attended testified that they had previously donated money to the association and that the donation receipts had been lost due to the passage of time and could not be produced. Defendant Bei Runsheng testified that he had previously served as a director of the Foreign Goods Business Association but resigned in 1927. In 1931, he published a statement in the newspaper and submitted three copies of the newspaper as evidence. Zhang Lanping testified that he had served as a director of the Foreign Goods Business Association after 1927 and 1928. The affairs of the association were managed by four people, including President Xiang Rusong and Wang Xiaoxin. The Zhenxin Club was reorganized in 1929 and 1930, and the Renyi Association was reorganized in 1934. A general meeting was held beforehand, and it was reported to the City Party Department and the Social Affairs Bureau. The reason was that the association had always handled public welfare undertakings, but since each industry had established its own association, there was no need to continue handling public welfare affairs. Therefore, it was proposed to expand and reorganize the Renyi Charity Association. The property was previously managed by the Foreign Goods Business Association, then transferred to the Zhenxin Club after the reorganization, and then to the Renyi Charity Association after the reorganization of the Renyi Charity Association. However, the land for the association was initially purchased by Le Zhenbao. Due to the deed, it was under Le's name. It was previously kept by Bei Runsheng and is now kept by the Ruikang Firm. The money was deposited in Hengli Bank in relation to the association. At this point, the defendant's attorney, Yuan Hanyun, stated his opinion, asking whether the representative, Ma Shangjie,

Submitted a Letter of Authorization

Ma said that he would submit it tomorrow. He also asked whether the witnesses who attended today understood the situation of the case, whether they agreed to the lawsuit, and whether the lawsuit against the defendants was about a criminal matter or a property issue. Because the witness Wang Zuolin, who attended, is now a member of the executive committee of the Renyi Charity Association, there is no reason for him to sue himself. Zhang Lanping also testified that he did not manage the money in the association. When the association initially purchased the land, it was under Le Zhenbao's name because foreign merchants transferred the deed and needed an individual to come forward, so Le came forward. Also, when the association's

funds were insufficient in the beginning, Le helped to raise money. The court listened to the testimony and did not understand the situation of the land deeds in Shanghai. After the defendant's attorney, Yuan Hanyun, briefly described the history of purchasing land and transferring deeds through registration by foreign merchants in Shanghai concessions, the court asked the plaintiff's witness, Wang Zuolin, whether he held a position in the Renyi Charity Association. Wang replied that although the Renyi Charity Association elected him to be an executive committee member, he had not been there. Before the reorganization, a general meeting was held, but the number of people present was not enough to make a decision. The court then asked the defendant, Zhang Lanping, whether there were minutes of the meeting. Zhang replied that there was a summary and that he would have to look for it. Later, the court questioned the defendant, Le Zhenbao, who admitted that he handled the purchase of

the association's land. The land originally belonged to Wang Xiaoxin and was mortgaged to Dehe Foreign Firm for 2,000 pounds. Before the expiration of the mortgage, it was sold to the association. He handled the transaction and came forward to buy it, totaling three acres and six cents of land. He also handled the expiration of the mortgage, borrowing money from the Baojia Insurance Company to repay the mortgage. At that time, the association's donations were insufficient, so he helped to raise the money. The land deed is currently in his possession, and the deed is in Ruikang Firm. If either one is missing, it cannot be sold or mortgaged. The land was purchased during the Qing Guangxu era. After questioning this far, the court considered the case complex and needed to investigate the minutes of the Renyi Charity Association's reorganization meeting, the land deed of the Hengli Bank transaction, and other documents. The court announced that the hearing would be adjourned and would resume at 2:00 PM on the 18th. The court then adjourned.

The Case of Gan Weilu Refusing to Pay Municipal Taxes Ends

The case of lawyer Gan Weilu, who previously raised six reasons for refusing to pay property taxes, caused a sensation for a time. The Public Works Department entrusted three lawyers, Bo Liang, Ru Baoyi, and Shi Baoliang, to file a lawsuit with the First Special District Court. The Shanghai Garment Industry Trade Union was established in 1931. It has worked diligently and has made considerable progress over the years. Letter to the Editor

To the Editors,

In today's newspaper, the news item entitled "Pudong Waterworks Construction" mentions the situation of the Pudong Waterworks project and states that the plant is being implemented by the "Greater Shanghai Water Company." This is incorrect. The Pudong Waterworks is one of the projects under our management and is being handled by the Municipal Government. The plant is directly under our jurisdiction and there is no such thing as the "Greater Shanghai Water Company." Also, the news item was translated from the mainland press. When the reporter from that newspaper came to our company to interview us about the news, we answered in detail. The next day, when the newspaper published the article, it clearly wrote our company name as Greater Shanghai City Trust, and there was no mention of the "Greater Shanghai Water Company." We are deeply concerned that this will cause misunderstanding among the public and are therefore requesting that you correct this.

Sincerely,

General Affairs Department, Shanghai Industrial Trust, 25, , 11,

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday was as follows: The weather around Shandong is cloudy to clear, with northeast to southeast winds. The Yellow River Basin has southwest winds. The upper reaches of the Yangtze River have light winds of uncertain direction. The weather in the middle reaches is changing from overcast to cloudy, gradually clearing, with northwest to northeast winds. The weather in the lower reaches and the East China Sea is cloudy to clear, with light northeast to southeast winds. The hurricane in the Pacific Ocean is still slowly moving north. At 2:00 PM, its center was within 120 miles of 20 degrees north latitude and 128 degrees east longitude, lingering without moving or moving very slowly. The wind strength is unknown. The hurricane near Guam Island will move west-northwest. Also, in the 24 hours prior to 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 82.0 degrees and the lowest was 64.4 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 94.5 degrees and the lowest was 76.1 degrees.

Educational News

Executive Yuan Orders Emphasis on National Children's Education and Health: Orders the Two Ministries of Interior and Education and the Department of Health to Expedite the Planning of Agencies for Children's Welfare

(Nanjing, November 11th) The Executive Yuan ordered the Ministry of Interior to investigate that children's welfare has more than one aspect, and that the most important aspects are children's education and children's health. Recent surveys of the Beijing-Tianjin area found that there are more than 20,000 children out of school. The total number of children out of school nationwide is more than 30 million. The number is shockingly high. In recent years, the collapse of the rural economy and the inability of farmers' children to attend school are important reasons. However, there are too few elementary schools in various places. If all school-age children were to enroll, there would not be enough space. At present, there are no concrete relief measures for the problem of school-age children who are out of school, and thus there is no way to urge and emphasize physical education and health. At present, the agency responsible for children's welfare has not yet been established, and the above two points cannot be delayed. The Ministry of Interior, together with the Ministry of Education and the Department of Health, should quickly plan and implement measures to promote it.

The new library of Aurora University in this city has been fully completed. The opening ceremony is scheduled for 4:00 PM today. The French book exhibition, which has been in preparation for a long time, will also open at the same time. The details are as follows:

Opening Ceremony of the New Library

The school previously found that the original library had a growing number of books and was insufficient. Therefore, last summer, it began construction of a four-story building in the west campus of the school. In addition to a portion of the building being used as the university's office and the law school's lecture hall, the remaining portion was used for the library. Construction has been underway for more than a year and was fully completed last month. The opening ceremony is scheduled to be held in the new library at 3:00 PM this afternoon, and guests from all walks of life are invited to visit.

French Exhibition Opens Today

It is expected that there will be a grand occasion at that time.

The Recent Four Years of National Central University (6)

— Luo Jialun

17. Advocating Research and Encouraging Academic Publications

For faculty members who are interested in engaging in specialized research, we have spared no effort in providing the necessary equipment and facilities to the best of our ability. We also aim to publish the results of their research to gain recognition from the international academic community for our university. In the past four academic years, we have published four series of journals: the Literary Series, the Education Series, and the Agricultural Series, each of which has reached Volume 3, Issue 1; the Social Sciences Series has reached Volume 2, Issue 2. Additionally, we have published more than ten types of scientific reports and other academic research reports, some of which have been translated into German or English and have received praise from the international academic community. Although these are just initial results, there will certainly be a day in the future when they will continue to be promoted and developed.

18. Striving for Cooperation with Academic Institutions and Integrating with National and Social Undertakings. Over the past four years, whenever the nation and society have needed to develop undertakings, our university has done its best to assist, proceeding with cooperation and considering its capacity. For example, we have helped the Huai River Commission analyze the soil in the Huai River basin, assisted the military authorities in surveying oil in Sichuan, undertaken afforestation for the capital's fortresses, sent personnel to the Yunnan border to investigate biology, co-organized the Yunnan Border Geographical Survey Team with the Resources Committee, co-organized cotton training classes with the National Economic Council, co-organized the Jiangpu Cotton Planting Guidance Center with the Central Cotton Improvement Institute, surveyed the geology of the entire Jiangning Autonomous Experimental County, improved silkworm and wheat varieties, designed electric irrigation, and assisted in the operation of agricultural improvement projects in experimental townships. We have jointly carried out rice, wheat, cotton, and miscellaneous grain experiments in more than twenty locations with agricultural experiment stations in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Hunan, Sichuan, and other provinces and counties; cooperated with the Ministry of Health and the Nanjing Municipal Government to run health clinics and hygiene experiment services; cooperated with the Ministry of Industry to compile Chinese economic statistics; cooperated with the Yangtze River Water Conservancy Commission to conduct hydraulic engineering experiments; investigated English teaching materials in secondary schools nationwide for the China Foundation for the Promotion of Education and Culture; and operated a consultation center for children's issues for the National Children's Year Implementation Committee. These are all verifiable examples. Furthermore, the establishment of the Educational Experiment Institute, the Economic Data Room, and the Administrative Research Data Room within the university are all preparations to train students to research current practical problems, in order to make the national university education somewhat beneficial to the national economy and the people's livelihood.

However, our university's current location is in the center of the city, surrounded by streets on all sides, with an area of only over two hundred mu. It is cramped and narrow, leaving no room for development, which causes the College of Agriculture to be separated from the main part of the university, making teaching facilities extremely uneconomical. Various agricultural experiment fields are also scattered in different locations, not together with the various departments, creating many difficulties in terms of experimental research. At the same time, various experimental factories urgently need to be added to the College of Engineering, including the experimental factories for special machinery research classes, all of which require a large area. The facilities for pathology, anatomy, and clinical diagnosis at the College of Medicine also have no space to accommodate them, making it difficult to proceed. As for the housing problem for faculty and students, it is especially necessary to provide adequate solutions to ensure the physical and mental well-being of educators. All of these are urgent needs based on facts and cannot be delayed. As for being mixed in with the city, which is not suitable for cultivating a noble and pure academic atmosphere, the principle is self-evident and there is no need to elaborate further. Fortunately, this matter has been approved by the government, and a decision has been made to actively proceed, first expanding and rebuilding the Colleges of Engineering, Agriculture, and Science, which are in the most urgent need of facilities, to support the central government's original intention of promoting practical science education and to meet the current urgent needs of the country. Moreover, the current location of the College of Physical Education has been traversed and divided by the newly opened Fujian, Chahar, Heilongjiang, and other roads. The special equipment and factories of the College of Engineering also urgently need to be expanded and added. All of these are pressing issues. Fortunately, the location of the new campus has been determined after many surveys, near Shizigang on Jingjian Road outside Zhonghua Gate. It has been approved by the government. The area faces Zijin Mountain to the north, connects to Niushou Mountain to the south, leans against Fang Mountain to the east, and looks out over the Yangtze River to the west from a high vantage point. The future construction area within the campus will be surrounded by mountains, with a small river crossing in front, lush trees, and extremely beautiful scenery. It is truly an ideal place for academic research. Moreover, it is still in the urban area, only three or four kilometers from the city, and not isolated from the city. It simply seeks a location on the periphery of the city that allows for concentrated research, adequate facilities, and expansion at any time. Furthermore, with its convenient transportation, it can still maintain cooperative relationships with various cultural, academic, and health institutions in the capital. As for all matters related to building construction, equipment, and the custody and distribution of funds, it has been approved that the Ministry of Education establish a Construction and Equipment Committee to take charge. The selection of personnel will be approved and hired by the Ministry of Education, and those with knowledge and experience from outside institutions will be invited to participate in the guidance to show prudence and impartiality.

The above are just the major points. There are still many incomplete and imperfect areas. I hope that wise people will provide guidance and assistance, which will not only be the good fortune of National Central University. (End)

News from the Ministry of Education's Literacy Education Cadre Training Class

In order to train cadres in various provinces and cities to handle literacy education, the Ministry of Education has decided to hold a literacy education cadre training class in Beijing starting on September 20 this year. It has previously ordered the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities to select administrative personnel in charge of literacy education and personnel currently serving or preparing to be appointed as heads of literacy teacher training classes to come to Beijing for training. Currently, more than twenty provinces and cities have submitted lists of personnel coming to Beijing. The Ministry of Education has also arranged the curriculum and hired lecturers. The curriculum is divided into (1) Spiritual Lectures, (2) Military Common Sense, (3) Administrative Issues in Compulsory Education, (4) Recent Trends in Education, (5) Rural Economy, (6) School Hygiene and Public Health, (7) Overview of the Implementation of Compulsory Education in Various Countries, (8) Mass Education and Compulsory Education, (9) Special Lectures, and visits, totaling 179 hours. The training will last for one and a half months, ending on November 5. The lecturers are Chen Jianxiao, Yu Ziyi, Chen Heqin, Zheng Xiaocang, Lu Yiyan, Yang Xiaochun, Li Buqing, Ma Ketan, Zhang Zonglin, Zhuang Zeyi, Chang Daozhi, Tang Qiyu, Zhu Ligeng, Jin Baoshan, Gu Shusen, Ma Zongcha, Chen Lijiang, Chen Shizhen, Dai Xia, Gu Zhaochen, Dai Yingguan, Tang Xifen, Wu Yan'yin, Wang Wanzhong, Zhong Daozan, Zhou Bangdao, etc. Key figures from the Party and the nation will also be invited to give special lectures. Yesterday, the Ministry appointed Gu Shusen as the director of the class, Tang Cuo as the deputy director, Zhou Bangdao as the director of academic affairs, Zhang Jiong and Tang Xifen as the training committee members, Yu Dehui as the director of administrative affairs, and Zhang Xingjian, Pan Pingzhi, Xu Zicheng, Shi Wei, and Peng Shuren as staff members. In addition, Liu Jianqun was hired as the chairman of the Training Committee. As the 20th is a Sunday, the class will begin on the 21st.

Xiao Wuquan's Painting Exhibition Opens Today

The contemporary master painter Xiao Wuquan, recently persuaded by dozens of friends including Ye Yuhu, Zhang Shizhao, Zhao Shuru, Li Haoran, and Li Bake, has put out more than two hundred of his most satisfactory works for a painting exhibition at the Ningbo Fellow Association on Tibet Road in this city, starting today (the 12th) for three days. Mr. Xiao has lectured in the north and south, and is over seventy years old, but his spirit is vigorous. His late-year works are extremely precious, with elegant colors and rhythms, and strong and profound brushstrokes, truly works to be passed down to future generations. It is heard that Mr. Xiao's disciples Jiang Danshu, Xi Tuge, Zhang Sun, Meng Lu, Shi Chongpeng, etc., all have works participating.

Chen Jianmin Discusses National Defense and Mental Science

Chen Jianmin of the China Mental Science Research Association discusses that the key to national defense, in the active aspect, is the development of combat power. The power of combat, on one hand, relates to weapons and physique, but fundamentally relies entirely on mental action for its transformation. "The best strategy is to attack the mind," as the ancient saying goes. The power of matter is small, and the power of the mind is great. Dr. Sun Yat-sen has already shown this to the public in his speeches on the spiritual education of soldiers. Today, military officers often pay attention to the preparation of material conditions. I sincerely hope that the army, in addition to technical training, will also supplement it with mental training. Regarding the mental training of soldiers, this association is currently drafting a concrete plan and will soon submit it to the military authorities for adoption. This is regarding the active aspect. As for the passive aspect, it is still necessary to prevent the reduction of combat power. If soldiers are injured or become ill, although ordinary military doctors are responsible for treatment, once wartime mental or neurological diseases occur, spiritual therapy must be used, but currently there are no specialized doctors in our country's army. During the European War, the Higher Neurological Hospital of France first adopted spiritual therapy, and at that time, British psychologist Dr. Brown was hired as a medical officer to specialize in treating this disease, with the most significant results. Dr. Brown alone cured more than three thousand wartime mental and neurological patients in the hospital using spiritual therapy. The number of such sick soldiers in other hospitals is not included. It can be seen that this disease is important in wartime. Therefore, mental science has a significant relationship to any aspect of national defense. I sincerely hope that the people of the country will rise up and study it, etc.

(V) (IX) Ninth Day of the Games

The ninth day of the Games saw the complete end of the track and field events, and the start of the swimming events, with finals in some categories. The schedule for the day was as follows: 9:00 AM Fencing, Swimming, Rowing; 10:00 AM Wrestling; 3:00 PM Track and Field (Marathon Final, Women's High Jump Final, Men's 400m Relay Final, Men's 1600m Relay Final, Women's 400m Relay Final), Swimming; 4:00 PM Basketball; 4:10 PM German Gymnastics Performance; 4:30 PM Hockey; 7:00 PM Wrestling; 8:00 PM Fencing. The results and records of the track and field and swimming events are as follows:

Track and Field

Marathon Final

The marathon final was held at 3:00 PM. The starting and finishing points were both in the Games stadium. There were 52 runners at the start, but 10 dropped out midway, so only 42 completed the entire course. Japanese athlete Son Kitei remarkably won the championship with a time of 2 hours, 29 minutes, 19.2 seconds, breaking the Games record (set by the previous champion, Zabala of Argentina, at 2 hours, 31 minutes, 36 seconds). Another Japanese athlete, Nan Shoryu, won third place, with the same time as the second-place British athlete, Hapen, only a shoulder's length behind. When the news spread, the whole city of Berlin was stirred. Only two of the three long-distance runners from Finland managed to secure fourth and fifth place, and the other one was eliminated. The previous champion, Zabala of Argentina, who had been leading the way up to 28,000 meters, withdrew due to exhaustion at 31,000 meters, which was also unexpected. Our Chinese athlete, Wang ZhengLin, fought hard and, although he finished in 40th place, it was no easy feat to complete the entire course. Wang's time was 3 hours, 15 minutes, 36.4 seconds, almost an hour behind the first-place winner.

Son Kitei (Japan) 2 hours, 29 minutes, 19 seconds

Hapen (England) 2 hours, 30 minutes, 23.2 seconds

Nan Shoryu (Japan) Same as above

Taimila (Finland) 2 hours, 32 minutes, 45 seconds

Munanen (Finland) 2 hours, 33 minutes, 46 seconds

Kaurman (South Africa) 2 hours, 36 minutes, 17 seconds

Women's High Jump Final

The women's high jump final was held at 3:00 PM with a total of 17 participants. The qualifying height was set at 1.60 meters, with the starting height at 1.30 meters. One person failed to clear it. When the height was raised to 1.40 meters, another three were eliminated. At 1.50 meters, another five stepped down. Then, at 1.55 meters, another three were eliminated. At 1.58 meters, another two were eliminated. Only three people cleared 1.60 meters. As a result, Szak of Hungary took first place with a jump of 1.62 meters, which was 0.03 meters short of the Games and world record of 1.65 meters set by the previous champion, Healy of the United States. It was a novel situation in all sports that only three jumpers were ranked in this competition.

(1) Szak (Hungary) 1.62 meters

(2) Oldham (England) 1.60 meters

(3) Kahl (Germany) 1.60 meters

Men's 4x100m Relay Final

At 2:10 PM, the men's 400-meter relay final saw the US team still fielding Owens, Metcalfe, Tellep, and Wykoff. Owens ran the first leg, finishing the 100 meters with a lead of three meters over the other teams. Metcalfe continued, and by the end of 200 meters, the lead had increased to six meters. Tellep gained another meter, and when Wykoff took the baton and finished, the lead was over ten meters. They broke the 40-second barrier, setting a new world record with 39.8 seconds (the US team set the previous record of 40 seconds in 1932). The Netherlands team was originally in second place, but the last runner accidentally fell upon receiving the baton, resulting in disqualification, which was a great pity.

(1) United States 39.8 seconds

(2) Italy 41.1 seconds

(3) Germany 41.2 seconds

(4) Argentina 42.7 seconds

(5) Canada 42.7 seconds

Women's 4x100m Relay Final

The women's 400-meter relay final was held at 3:30 PM. Great Britain was in the innermost lane, followed by Italy, the United States, Germany, Canada, and the Netherlands. Germany had the most balanced talent and the strongest overall strength. The first three runners for Germany led all the way, with the United States lagging behind by four or five meters. However, the last runner for Germany accidentally fell upon receiving the baton, ruining all their efforts. Ms. Dowflerite covered her face and wept, filled with sorrow and anger. The last runner for the US team, Ms. Stephens, used her final sprint to reach the finish line first with a time of 46.9 seconds, equaling the Games record set by the US team at the previous Games. Great Britain finished second, five meters behind.

First place: United States 46.9 seconds

Second place: Great Britain 47.6 seconds

Third place: Canada 47.8 seconds

Sweden was in the innermost lane, Germany in the second lane, Hungary in the third lane, the United States in the fourth lane, Canada in the fifth lane, and Great Britain in the outermost lane. In the end, Great Britain defeated the United States by eight meters, which was no easy feat. The first runner for Great Britain took the lead immediately, and the speed of the subsequent two runners was also very consistent. By the time Brown took the last leg, the lead over the US team was already seven meters. Although Frederick made every effort to catch up, it was to no avail. The time for the British team was 3 minutes and 9 seconds, which was still far from the world and Games record set by the US team in the previous Games (3 minutes, 8.2 seconds).
