Hao Ming, Li Qingan, and Wu Bixian Return to China from Germany and Arrive in Tianjin; Impressions of Germany are Extremely Favorable; Delegation to Arrive in Shanghai on the 27th

(Tianjin Dispatch) Our country's athletes and inspection team participating in the World Games, led by Mr. Wang Zhengting, arrived in Italy on the 4th and took the Conte Rosso back to China. It is estimated that they will arrive in Shanghai around the 27th of this month. In addition to Chief Secretary Shen Siliang, who passed through Tianjin on the 3rd and arrived in Shanghai on the 6th, it is now known that the national team coach Hao Ming, basketball team manager Li Qingan, and high jumper Wu Bixian took the Siberian Railway back to China from Germany in late last month and arrived in Tianjin on the morning of the 6th. After a day of rest, they attended banquets hosted by various parties yesterday. Wu Bixian is scheduled to go to Shanghai in the coming days. Hao and Li expressed their immense admiration for the German preparations for the World Games, the completeness of the facilities, the thoroughness of the hospitality, and the general spirit of service and good discipline of the German people. They said that there are many aspects of German society that our country can learn from, while there are many questionable aspects of our country's officials, athletes, and inspection team members in terms of spirit, physique, etiquette, and actions.

(Beiping Dispatch) Our country's World Games delegation is scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on the 27th of this month. The delegation's training, entertainment, and other committees have concluded their work. After the delegates arrive in Shanghai, they will return to their respective hometowns. Yuan Dunli, Li Zhou, Xia Xiang, Zhao Wenzao, and others are expected to arrive in Beiping on the 30th. Ma Dehan, Dong Shouyi, and Xu Minghui will stay in Germany to study physical education and will go to the United States next summer and return to China in the fall. Shen Siliang, the general secretary of the National Sports Federation, has returned to Shanghai. In order to finalize all income and expenditure accounts related to attending the World Games in Germany and prepare for the training for the 1940 World Games, it is planned to convene a board meeting at the end of the month. The Japanese athletes' delegation received much praise at this World Games. They will perform when passing through Shanghai, and the National Sports Federation will prepare for the reception.

(VI)(X) Two Major Battles of Basketball in the Fourth Week

As the Games basketball competition entered its fourth week, only eight teams remained, divided into four groups for competition. Among them, the most attention was naturally focused on the United States versus the Philippines and Canada versus Uruguay (the other two groups were Mexico defeating Italy 34-17, and Poland defeating Peru, Peru surrendering). These two matches were moved to the large basketball court. The United States versus the Philippines was at 5:00 PM, and Canada versus Uruguay was at 6:00 PM. However, Europeans' interest in basketball was not as enthusiastic as in other sports, so there were only a thousand spectators for these two exciting battles.

The United States Team Thoroughly Defeats the Philippines

The United States is the birthplace of basketball and has excellent skills, which goes without saying. However, the Philippines has long been the hegemon of the Far East, and its strength should not be underestimated. Although the outcome of the game was largely determined before the start, it was generally believed that the Philippines would pose a great threat to the United States. Indeed, in the first half, the Philippine team fought with all its might and was only eight points behind. In the second half, the US team relied on its tall stature and quick movements to put on a spectacular performance. The Philippine team was unable to retaliate and was completely defeated.

At the referee's command, the two teams lined up facing the center circle. The American center, Fodenbree, was six feet tall, while the Philippine player, Macson, was a head shorter. The American team had the advantage in the center jump. After two or three passes, the left guard, Huiz Wanlai, charged into the Philippine camp and raised his hand, sending the ball straight through the net to open the scoring. Fodenbree's long shot missed, but the right forward, Johnson, rushed up and tapped the ball in for another score. The Philippine team got the ball and launched a counterattack. The left forward, Burke, tried his skills under the basket and scored. Fodenbree rebounded under the basket as easily as reaching into a bag and lightly put the ball in. Six to two, the US team took the lead. After Knowles and Martinez each scored one point for their respective teams from free throws, Fodenbree and Johnson scored again, making it eleven to three, further widening the gap. The Philippine team launched a desperate counterattack. After Martinez scored on a free throw, Padiera and Macson successively broke through the final defense line and pulled back four points. Burke missed two free throws, which was a big blow. In contrast, the American team's morale was doubled, and they fought more and more bravely. Huiz Tolai showed his skills, and Fodenbree was also accurate from a distance. Although Padiera sneaked in a goal in the American camp, Swanson made two decisive long shots, making it nineteen to ten. The Philippine army changed its strategy, passing the ball on the ground, making it difficult for the American army to bend down. Burke and Padiera broke through the net twice, and the American army hurriedly replaced Shi Huangsheng with Lageran, making the back line more stable. The three forwards emerged in the enemy's camp, with a strong momentum. The Philippine team struggled to follow, indomitable. At halftime, the Americans narrowly won 28 to 20. In the break, the Philippine team's physical strength was insufficient and it had become exhausted, while the Americans had more than enough strength and became braver and braver. The defense was as solid as a golden wall, and the front line was like entering an uninhabited land. With continuous penalties and scores, they added nine points. Only then did Martinez score one point for the Philippine team with a free throw. After that, the American army bombarded continuously, adding thirteen points, directly causing the Philippine team to be dizzy and unable to resist. Burke worked hard to steal a goal under the basket, but Johnson and Knowles repeatedly crushed it. In the second half, the American army still scored twenty-eight points, while the Philippine army only scored three points. As a result, the United States won 56 to 23. The referee was Islan.

Finance: Major Players Watching, Gold Prices Hover in a Short Range

Women's Special

Sudden Tightening of Buying Sentiment in Afternoon Market Causes Cotton Prices to Rise

Initially, the cotton market saw a downward trend due to clear weather and weakness in foreign cotton prices. However, rumors circulated that prices were high in various production areas, with reports of a two-dollar price surge for Ningbo Yao cotton. Consequently, short sellers rushed to cover their positions, causing market prices to rebound.

Spot Cotton Prices Rise by Another Four Jiao

In the early market for spot cotton, prices initially rose following the rise in US cotton, but then fell. The result was mixed, fluctuating between one and nine points. Indian cotton fell by 1.25 rupees, and Osaka's Sanpin cotton fell by 0.34 jiao. The local weather cleared up with a cool breeze, dampening sentiment somewhat. Buying interest in the market was not strong, and prices for all months fell by 0.23 jiao. However, floating traders covered their positions later, causing prices to fluctuate by 0.05 to 0.10 jiao. Chengji, Dafu, Yuda, Mingde, Gengfeng, Xingchang, Tonghe, and Shengyuan all sold, while Changhe made a strong effort to buy 10,000 dan. Runkang, Yongchang, Dafeng, Changfeng, and Xincheng covered shorts and increased positions. As a result, prices for all months fell by 0.23 jiao compared to the previous day's close. The afternoon market opened with extremely tight conditions. Rumors that a certain bank's general manager was about to assume an important financial position spurred a rush to buy, driving prices up across the board. As a result, prices for all months rose by 0.55 to 0.65 jiao compared to the morning close. Chengji sold 10,000 dan, Dafu 9,000 dan, Deda 3,400 dan, Shenji 3,300 dan, Taichang 4,500 dan, Xincheng 3,800 dan, Yichang 2,600 dan, Xingchang 2,600 dan, Shengyuan 2,400 dan, and Tonghe 3,100 dan. Fukang bought 5,000 dan, Dachang 2,500 dan, Dafeng 2,300 dan, Dachangcheng 4,700 dan, Runkang 8,400 dan, Yongchang 3,100 dan, Changhe 10,500 dan, Hexing 3,000 dan, Fengtai 4,200 dan, and Renfeng 5,000 dan. The highest and lowest prices of the day are listed on the left.

Cotton Merchants Hoarding, Transactions Gradually Decreasing

The consumption of spot cotton is mediocre. Holders are asking for prices that are too high, making it difficult for buyers and sellers to agree. 3,200 bales of Yao cotton arrived, with an asking price of 34.20 yuan.

Lingbao Cotton 58.25 Yufeng Factory Purchase 170 pieces Delivery to factory in October/November

Lingbao Cotton 55.50 Yufeng Factory Purchase 173 pieces Spot delivery to factory

Lingbao Cotton 55.75 Yufeng Factory Purchase 65 pieces Spot delivery to factory

Local Stocks of Chinese and Japanese Yarn Sharply Reduced by Over 14,000 Bales

A certain cotton industry organization in this port investigated the yarn inventory of Chinese and Japanese factories in Shanghai as of the end of August. The inventory of Japanese yarn was 3,742 bales, and the inventory of Chinese yarn was 54,425 bales, totaling 58,167 bales. This is a decrease of 14,016 bales compared to the 72,183 bales at the end of July, with Japanese yarn decreasing by 946 bales and Chinese yarn decreasing by 13,070 bales. The breakdown of yarn inventory is recorded below (unit: bales):

(Note: The more than 30,000 bales of 20-count yarn stored in the Yarn and Fabric Exchange warehouse are also included in the calculation.)

US Cotton Market Prices Nearly Firm in the Near Term, Weak in the Long Term

Yesterday, US cotton opened with prices ranging from unchanged to up two points. Early in the morning, due to cotton farmers selling short at the previous day's close, trading was hesitant. Later, due to buying by dealers and Liverpool, prices rose. Short positions in near-term months were mostly shifted to long-term months, resulting in near-term firmness and long-term weakness. Before the close, increased short selling led to a gradual correction. The market is currently quiet, and the close was stable. Spot prices were unchanged, while futures prices fell by nine points to up three points. English spot cotton fell by four points, and futures fell by 12 points. The liquidation of long positions in Indian cotton was absorbed by short covering. Later, cotton merchants bought across different months, which was then overturned by the liquidation of long positions. Pingguoer fell by 1.25 rupees, Aomula fell by one rupee, and Bairoxi fell by 1.25 rupees. Original telegrams are recorded on the left (dated the 11th):

Pingguoer 157.75 Down 1.25 18.80

Aomula 196.00 Down 1.00 35.20

Bairoxi 118.75 Down 1.25 39.80

According to a telegram from Bombay, the opening forecast for the 11th was: Bairoxi at 218.5 rupees, down 0.25 rupees; Aomula at 196 rupees, unchanged from the previous day; and Pingguoer at 158 rupees, up 0.25 rupees.

Yarn and Cotton Both Fall: Telegram from Osaka on the 11th. Sanpin futures yarn fell by 0.60 to 1.20 yuan, with near-term at 215 yuan and long-term at 203.8 yuan. Futures cotton fell by 0.15 to 0.35 jiao, with near-term at 66.6 yuan and long-term at 64.45 yuan.

Grains: Some Outside Buying Interest, Flour Prices Initially Decline then Rebound

Yesterday in the flour market, prices for all months were generally flat after the morning opening. Although quoted prices for imported wheat saw a slight improvement, actual sales in the northern routes remained sluggish. Therefore, trading was sideways. Compared to the previous day's closing price, prices fell by about 0.075 yuan. The afternoon opening saw little movement initially, but later, due to outside buying interest, there was a slight increase in buying. Factory hedging was also largely on the sidelines. Therefore, although trading was not brisk, asking prices rose by nearly a full yuan. Industry insiders speculate that if northern sales remain as sluggish as usual during the current peak sales season, and factories accumulate inventory, there may be downward pressure in the near future.

Wheat Market Quiet Initially, Afternoon Slightly Better Due to Buying by Hankou Dealers

Yesterday, the wheat market was quiet as usual during the morning opening. Few asking prices showed any improvement, and were roughly the same as the previous day. During the afternoon opening, however, trading was more active and buying interest increased. It was rumored that dealers from Hankou were buying because wheat prices there had risen. Standard wheat saw a slight increase in buying, and sentiment strengthened slightly, improving by 0.01 yuan compared to the previous day. Current wheat prices remained stable, and factory demand was relatively weak. Prices were quoted as follows: Kaiming Guangwu River wheat at 4.95 yuan, Zhuzhen wheat at 4.76 yuan, Suqian wheat at 4.86 yuan (discount of 0.082 yuan), Jiangbei wheat at 4.77 yuan (secondary grade at 4.63 yuan), Jiangjiaba wheat at 4.83 yuan (discount of 0.08 yuan), Gaoyou wheat at 4.7224 yuan, Wuyi wheat at 4.83 yuan, Nanjing wheat at 4.75 yuan, Yaowan wheat at 4.89 yuan, and Taizhou wheat at 4.78 yuan. Fuxin bought 3,000 bags, Fufeng bought 1,500 bags, and Shenda bought 1,000 bags.

Ke Xian Initially Weak then Stable, Guangdong Dealers Stop Buying While Shantou Continues Strongly

Yesterday, arrivals of Ke Xian rice remained strong. New arrivals from Sha, Han, Xiang, and Gan totaled 20,000 bags, while existing inventory in the market reached over 100,000 bags. Due to ample supply from production areas and continuous arrivals, the market was inherently weak. Guangdong dealers were buying actively, which helped support the market. Yesterday, however, Guangdong dealers stopped buying because their previous orders had not yet been fully loaded, and due to tonnage and market price considerations. The market became soft and listless again, and prices seemed to be trending downward. Fortunately, Shantou dealers continued to buy actively, and local buying interest was also strong, which helped support the market. Local dealers also responded by selling 600-700 bags of coarse rice. The market stabilized in a weak position. A total of 4,720 bags of Jiangxi rice, 3,453 bags of Xiang rice, 300 bags of Han coarse rice, and 250 bags of Taiwan Xian rice were sold throughout the day.

He Xia Rice Market Remains Weak as Before

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, arrivals from various dealers increased compared to the previous day, totaling over 5,000 shi (a unit of dry measure) from 25-26 sources. However, local sales were sluggish. Although Qingdao and Dalian dealers bought over 500 bags, the market was still difficult to maintain. Prices for thick and thin Japonica rice fell slightly. Although arrivals of Dongxin Japonica rice were not strong, the 5 shi of newly arrived Kunshan rice in the northern market inevitably had an impact, lowering prices by 0.1 yuan. Du Yang and other newly harvested varieties saw weaker sales and shorter measurements. The Yin variety was mediocre.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, there were 34-35 arrivals from various sources in He Xia. Sales of cheaper varieties were slightly better, while prices for high-quality broken Japonica rice were weak and unchanged. New West Japonica rice was down by 0.1-0.2 yuan, Dongxin Japonica rice was down by 0.1 yuan, Chen Yangjian rice was down slightly. The Bianyuan variety was stable. New Yangjian rice was up slightly, Xin Tuanjian rice was up slightly, and Xin Bujien rice was down by 0.1-0.2 yuan. Thin Indica rice was down by 0.1 yuan.

Fuxin bought 3,000 bags, Fufeng bought 1,500 bags, and Shenda bought 1,000 bags.

Japanese Merchants Actively Buying Rapeseed Causes Prices to Rise Sharply: Secondary Grade Soybeans Still in Demand by Factories

Rapeseed trading has a new outlet in Japan. The market was not expected to develop significantly, but recently, due to the rise in prices of all kinds of oil raw materials, rapeseed has become an important commodity for that country. Therefore, buying interest has been very strong, and market prices have been rising steadily. Earlier this month, Pinghu rapeseed rose from 9.89 yuan to 10.01 yuan, with over 2,000 bags traded. Yesterday, prices rose again to 10.02 yuan, with 1,000 bags traded. Currently, only a small amount of Pinghu rapeseed is available on the market, so the price increase remains quite sharp. New soybeans saw balanced arrivals and sales, and prices were largely unchanged. A total of over 3,700 bags of various soybeans were sold. High-quality beans commanded high prices, so factories only bought middle- to upper-grade beans. The future trend is currently difficult to predict.

North-South Goods: First Batch of New Xinghua Longan Arrives, Over 3,000 Pieces; Shizhuang Goods Plunge by Six Yuan

Recently, arrivals of new longan have been increasing gradually. The first batch of new Xinghua longan also arrived yesterday, with over 3,000 boxes. Therefore, quoted prices tended to soften, falling by varying amounts of 2-3 yuan. Over 1,600 boxes were traded. At the same time, in order to promote sales, dealers reduced the prices of Shizhuang goods, such as Dingji Tianji Tianhong, by six yuan across the board. It is said that sun-dried longan pulp also fell by about three yuan.

Xu Kuizi in Short Supply, Prices Rise Again by Four Jiao: A New North Goods Store Opens... Chen Da

Recently, Xu Kuizi has been in short supply in production areas, leading to repeated price increases in the market. Prices rose again by 0.04 yuan recently, reaching 18.20 yuan. Premium-grade Zhuangzi was priced at over 19 yuan. Small packages also saw prices rise in tandem. Industry sources report that Li Nifeng, the former manager of Houde, has newly established a large North Goods store named Chen Da. The store is located on Yanghang Street, at the original site of Houde.

Sugar Market: Zhenji Refined White Sugar Down Slightly by 0.1 Yuan

Yesterday, the sugar market trended stable. The association's quoted price for spot No. 24 coarse granulated white sugar fell slightly by 0.05 yuan to 21.55 yuan, with some transactions. Transshipment goods were quoted up by 0.05 yuan, but no deals were made. High-grade Zhuang was priced at 6.6 yuan, ordinary grade at 6.55 yuan, and Dongbai No. 4 trademark transshipment goods at 6.3 yuan, and No. 8 at 6.1 yuan, all seeing slight increases. Zhenji refined white sugar from local factories was down slightly by 0.1 yuan, with No. 1 at 20.4 yuan, No. 2 at 20 yuan, No. 3 at 19.6 yuan, No. 4 at 19.2 yuan, and No. 5 at 18.8 yuan. There was a batch of wet brown sugar from the Chaozhou dealers, with Jisheng, Juyuan, and Maoye totaling over 170 bags at 15.1 yuan, Hechang and Zhangyi totaling 96 bags at 15 yuan, secondary grade Zhi 54 bags at 14.85 yuan, and Fuquanyang 40 bags at 18.1 yuan flat.

Yesterday was the third bidding session of the week for sugar from joint-stock companies. The total quota was 8,365 bags. Bidding prices were largely unchanged, except for high-quality sugar from Quxi Factory, which was bid up by 0.1 yuan but failed to sell. ShunDe Factory's Wuyang coarse white sugar sold 1,305 bags at 21.4 yuan, Quxi Factory sold another 220 bags at 20.7 yuan, Shixin Factory sold another 135 bags at 21.2 yuan, and medium granulated white sugar sold 70 bags at 19.3 yuan. A total of 1,730 bags were traded.

Women Should Strive for Equal Opportunities to Serve in Society

— Zhenhua

Since the rise of the women's movement, women in all aspects of society have gained some benefits. However, because the atmosphere of fascism is becoming increasingly prevalent, and because the entire society's politics and economy are in a state of recession, the women's movement has also stagnated imperceptibly.

Women's demand for liberation and achieving equal status with men requires, as a first step, achieving equality in education and economics. This is a problem that everyone knows and is without doubt. However, if we obtain inheritance rights to property, possessing ample money; we acquire equal educational opportunities, creating advanced knowledge, but society does not allow us to utilize it, to practice it, then what use is something that we exchanged for after much effort and difficulty to us? Are we willing to lightly throw away what we have fought for? No, this is absolutely impossible. We should obtain equal opportunities for men and women to serve in society, and contribute what we have gained to society, so that all of humanity can be happy because of us.

However, things are not as easy as imagined, because with the increase in the number of unemployed, female employees who have just stepped onto the path of service, occupying the positions of male employees, they have to cry that women's work is like a vase, only for decoration. Of course, we cannot protect ourselves and absolutely oppose other people's criticisms, but we absolutely do not believe that every male employee has abundant knowledge? Able to serve loyally.

Sisters, we should understand that equality between men and women? It is by no means empty slogans that can be successful, we must use practical methods to fulfill it. Therefore, in society, we have to demand equality of opportunity for men and women to serve! To break the shackles of that parasitic life. But how do we obtain this equality? I think everything in the world is man-made, as long as everyone is willing to make up their minds, there is no reason why they cannot do it. Here are two points written down on my personal views.

(1) Cultivate a practical spirit. The success of a person depends entirely on persevering along a foolish path: opportunistic success is accidental and risky. Therefore, in the age of seeking, we cultivate a practical spirit, to acquire real knowledge, so that after academic achievement we can be employed by society, and when serving, we adhere to a practical spirit, and work hard, then, will we be dismissed?

(2) Get rid of flashy and vain decoration. Flashy and vain decoration not only consumes time and wastes money, but also easily provokes people's aversion and creates a psychology of contempt.

The two points mentioned above are not harsh demands. If we can do it, I believe that equal opportunities for men and women in social services can definitely be achieved and can last forever.

Biographies of Famous Women in the World (3)

— Lusha Bai

Varvara Yakovleva, who was as famous as Kollontai and served as the Soviet People's Commissar for Finance, was born in Moscow. She was a quiet and taciturn person with an amiable personality, completely different from Kollontai's outstanding and unrestrained character. She joined the party in 1904 and was arrested in 1910, sentenced to four years of exile. She escaped halfway and fled abroad. Two years later, she sneaked back into the country; in 1913, she was arrested again and exiled to Arkhangelsk for three years. She was also arrested and imprisoned several times in Moscow; it is rare to find a woman who has always fought to the end like her.

She was not as good at rhetoric as ordinary politicians, nor did she indulge in empty talk. She only knew how to immerse herself in practical work. Therefore, during her five years in office, she was able to abide by her duties and was highly trusted by the people of the country.

Nikolaeva came from a female worker in a bookbinding factory, and Alexandra Ardyutina rose from an apprentice in a tailoring shop to the head of the women's department of the Party Central Committee. She grew up in a poor family. Her mother was an uneducated textile worker. She only received elementary education at the age of ten, and then dropped out of school due to poverty to help her mother with work.

She spent her youth in this dim factory, completely isolated from all the joys of life and material enjoyment that life should have. Gnawing on black bread every day, she harbored a rebellious determination towards this accursed society. Different from intellectuals such as Kollontai and Yakovleva, she did not start from theory, but participated in the movement from her real life. She was elected as a cadre of the Petersburg Trade Union, and at the age of twenty, she had become an important party member. Before the October Revolution, she was arrested and imprisoned and sentenced to exile. Unlike ordinary women, who are full of sentimentality, the poor life in her childhood and the terrifying life of exile after participating in the revolution, tempered her into an iron-like character. There was no such thing as a woman's coquettishness or love between men and women in her at all.

A person with such a character can of course be regarded as a hero in troubled times, but when the Soviet Union entered the second five-year plan and social life had become relatively stable, a person like her had lost the meaning of her existence. She was elected as an alternate member of the Central People's Committee and the head of the women's department, and later promoted to the head of the women's department, but it has now been abolished. Her political status is also declining day by day.

A Type of French Human Figure in Japanese New Women's Side Jobs

— Hair

Japan was originally famous for making toys. When Japanese women have nothing to do at home, they make cloth foreign babies for their younger siblings to play with. The recently popular French portraits were learned from France. After research and improvement, it will become a unique Japanese toy again. At first, it was only for children to play with. Later, the manufacturing became exquisite and the materials became expensive. It has become a decoration for family rooms and a decoration for large store windows. The sales are very large, and the manufacturers have an income of two to three hundred yuan per month, so it has become a type of side job for new women in Japan.

The faces, hands and feet of ordinary foreign babies are not made of celluloid, but of porcelain clay, which is easy to break, dull and lifeless. And they are all made with complex machines, which are difficult to imitate in the family. The currently popular French portraits are all made of thin silk and colored satin. They are usually stored in wooden glass boxes, so they will remain intact for thousands of years.

The face of the human figure is the most difficult to manufacture. A thin piece of flesh-colored or white silk is pasted on several layers of gauze, and when it is damp, it is pressed in an iron mold. After drying, it becomes a beautiful oval face. The ears, nose, mouth and eyes are all painted with colors, so it is possible to imitate photos and draw all kinds of different faces. Most of them use movie stars and actresses as models. The model of a girl is of course the most lovely Shirley Temple. The size of the face is related to the length of the whole body, so there are many types of faces, which can be manufactured arbitrarily. The faces sold in stores range from 78 jiao to 12 yuan each. It is convenient and economical to manufacture them yourself at home.

The hair is made of raw silk, dyed in various colors, and can also be permed into curly waves. The limbs, hands, feet and body are also made of flesh-colored or white thin silk, with cotton stuffed in the middle, so they can be full and plump. Supported by various lead wires, a graceful curve is created. There is no definite standard for clothing decoration, and everything can be arranged as you like. This kind of French portrait was originally in the shape of foreign women, but now it can be changed into Japanese costumes, with high buns and kimonos, dragging a pair of small wooden exhibitions, which is quite interesting. If it is changed again into Chinese costumes, with short hair and cheongsam, I think it will definitely become popular in China. The basic method is the same, and it can be manufactured by any nation, regardless of gender or age.

The face, limbs and all the clothing, hats, shoes and ornaments of the human figure are all sold retail. If you can't make it yourself, you can buy the parts and assemble them yourself. And large companies hold lectures on a regular basis to teach methods, so more and more people are learning and becoming women's side jobs. The price of French human figures ranges from two or three yuan to several hundred yuan, and most of them are used for interior decoration and gifts. After being used as window decorations by stores, people passing by will stop to watch.

Women's Life on the Beach

— Mani

There are various opinions on the women's question in the current society. One says that women always rely on men, one says that men and women should share the burden of life, and another says that women should return to the family. I don't dare to talk nonsense about which problem is good. I don't want women to be used by merchants as commercial gimmicks, and I don't want women to rush to shovel five hundred times after returning to the family after dinner. Let's talk about women's life on the beach.

The women on the coast of the Yellow Sea are very miserable. Their husbands are mostly salt makers and fishermen. The living expenses they get are pitiful. How can they take care of their wives and children's food and drink? Most of the food is filled with sweet potato flour. Although their lives are so difficult, they don't complain about heaven or others. Because there are abundant aquatic products in the sea, they squat on the beach every day to pick fresh goods. It is said that "they can get four hundred texts a day. Because there are many children in the family, and men only earn a few hundred texts a day, so we do some easy work to supplement our lives."

It is also rare for women to voluntarily help their husbands in production like this, and their husbands do not have permanent jobs, but they can work all year round without stopping. Even in the autumn flood season, every time jellyfish are produced, there is no need to pick fresh ones, but cotton is planted in the fields, and people are needed to remove grass. So they hold iron shovels and rake grass under strong heat, and can get two yuan a day. Families with difficult lives can get subtle help, which is also a small supplement. Living by labor is not to starve. These women do not know a single word, and their minds are very simple. Moreover, in extremely difficult environments, selling labor to supplement their husbands' lives is a bit more meaningful than women in cities who only know how to eat, drink, and decorate themselves.

Marriage Customs in Abyssinia (Part 1)

— Wei Jing

Under the marriage system in Abyssinia, women have absolutely no right to choose their own destiny. A woman's marriage rights are entirely determined by her father. Once a father has promised his daughter to someone, it is as if he has already determined his daughter's fate, and he absolutely does not consider his daughter's wishes. One or two days before the daughter's marriage, the bride's father is required to prepare a feast. This feast usually consists of large amounts of raw beef, marinated mutton cooked in soy sauce, a mixture of oatmeal and butter, unleavened bread, etc. Among these items, strongly alcoholic drinks are usually added. While the bride's family is hosting such a grand banquet for the guests, the groom's relatives and friends are also enjoying the same banquet.

On the wedding day, the groom, accompanied by relatives and friends, rides a mule to the bride's house. To show their arrival, they must fire a volley of guns and perform a war dance. After that, they enter the bride's house in a large group. There, the bride's entire family (except for the bride), as well as relatives and friends, are waiting. After the groom arrives at the bride's house, the bride's family must prepare a seat for him. This seat is usually under an umbrella made of green grass. After taking his seat, the bride's family invites the groom to a feast (the dishes are similar to those mentioned above). After the feast, the relatives and friends who came with the groom must fire another volley of guns and perform another war dance. Then, the bride, wearing a long robe and a white thick cloth mask, is led in by the bridesmaids and sits on a pre-arranged long orange, listening quietly to her father reporting the dowry he is giving her. This dowry usually consists of livestock, furniture, farm tools, etc.

After the bride's father finishes his report, the groom and bride stand side by side under the umbrella, and the bride's father asks the groom if he is willing to take his daughter as his wife. The groom hooks his little finger with the bride's little finger, which signifies his willingness. The simple marriage is then completed. Next is the pastor's blessing. If a pastor cannot be found at the time, the blessing is performed by an older relative. After the blessing, dancing follows. Then the bride rides a mule to the groom's house, where another simple ceremony is held.

(To be continued)

Special feature of this newspaper

Ms. Deng Yuzhi Discusses Labor Welfare

— Ji Ping

In modern industrialized nations, there are sophisticated and comprehensive facilities for labor welfare. For example, if a certain industry only seeks short-term profits and ignores the safety, health, and hygiene of its workers, the result will inevitably be mutually destructive. China's industry cannot compare with industrialized countries, so labor welfare is also far behind. As the saying goes, "A rising tide lifts all boats," it may be premature to talk about how to handle these labor issues for the time being. However, everyone should understand the current situation of Chinese workers. I discussed this issue with Ms. Deng Yuzhi, who has been serving in the Labor Department of the National Association of Chinese Christian Women's Associations for ten years, and her remarks provide a glimpse into the situation.

Before discussing this topic, I must first introduce Ms. Deng's brief history to give readers an understanding. She is from Changsha, Hunan. After graduating from the Sociology Department of Ginling Women's College, she worked as a staff member in the Student Department of the Association. In less than three years, she was transferred to the Labor Department. In 1929, the Association sent her to Japan, Europe, and the United States to study labor welfare, with special attention to welfare work in the United Kingdom, the United States, Germany, Japan, and Switzerland. She spent five months and obtained a lot of valuable information. At that time, she wrote a lengthy report, but it was not published publicly. Upon arriving in England, she studied at the London School of Economics for another year and then returned to her original position. She has a thorough understanding of labor welfare and speaks frankly about it. I know readers will be very moved.

She said: "The labor conditions of various countries that I will discuss are from six years ago, but according to recent survey reports, there have been no major changes except in Germany, so I am bringing up old matters again: (1) At that time, Japanese labor unions were already very active, and their organizations were well-structured. The general education level of workers was higher than that of Chinese workers. The labor welfare provided by employers was not much different from that in the United Kingdom and the United States, such as worker relief, entertainment, food and lodging subsidies, education, etc., which were quite effective. (2) American labor unions were previously divided into two factions: one was the A.F.L., which consisted entirely of American-born workers, was conservative in its thinking, and discriminated against foreign workers, including Chinese workers. The other was the I.W.W., which treated foreign workers equally, was well-organized internally, and provided many educational, entertainment, and relief services for workers. Generally speaking, welfare services in American labor unions are divided into two types: one is organized by the factory, and the other is self-organized by the workers. The former stabilizes the lives of workers, eliminates the need to organize labor unions, reduces the consciousness of confrontation between labor and capital, and disperses the organizational strength of workers. The latter involves workers with higher intelligence who manage all welfare services themselves and do not want to be manipulated by employers in a planned manner. Both have their advantages and disadvantages. American industry is particularly developed, so worker welfare is better than in other countries. (3) At that time, German labor unions were very large. They ran their own newspapers and schools, from elementary school to university, which were very complete. Later, the political system changed, and now the power of the labor unions is controlled by the National Socialist Party, so the situation is certainly different now. I also examined the implementation of the British Factory Act. Their labor union organization is very strict, and worker education and training are no less than in the United States, but workers are not as active as in the United States, which shows the different national characteristics of the two countries.

Here, I want to talk about worker welfare in China, which can be divided into several points: (1) In China, it can be said that very few worker welfare programs are organized from the perspective of workers' own interests. Of course, we cannot compare with foreign countries. Foreign labor unions do not belong to any political party. Labor unions are a means of economic struggle for workers, such as fighting for wages and working hours, but they cannot escape political activities. (2) Everyone believes that implementing worker education and improving workers' intellectual level is an urgent matter, but the question of who should organize worker education is worth studying. In England, it is a third party in society, especially scholars who are enthusiastic about worker education, who organize worker education. In capitalist society, worker education is best done in England. You can talk to every worker about international issues or political issues, and they can answer well. I think even a middle school student would probably find it difficult. China now really needs a third party in society (neither the government nor the workers) to organize worker education. (3) Working hours in Chinese factories are longer than in any country. The usual is ten to twelve hours, and the treatment is very poor. Don't even mention education; even their health is not good. Their energy and time do not allow them to be baptized by education. Now the government wants to implement the Factory Act and reduce working hours, which is one of the important prerequisites. (4) Male workers suffer, but female workers suffer even more. According to statistics on workers in various industries, there are more female workers than male workers, and married female workers have household chores in addition to factory work. They often reduce their sleep time to complete their daily tasks. When it comes to before and after childbirth, they cannot take much leave, which makes them feel even more pain. In this situation, political power should be used to urge factories to run nurseries and extend maternity leave before and after childbirth, but this may not be easy to do, because factories also have their own difficulties, which makes them feel that employing female workers is a loss. As things stand, female workers themselves do not have healthy lives, which affects the physical condition of their children, which is a very serious problem. From the standpoint of the nation and the people, we cannot just let it pass. Because workers make up the largest majority of urban residents, if the workers' families are all unhealthy, the loss is terribly great. Disease is originally a painful thing in life, but the pain of poor and sick workers can be imagined. In a city as big as Shanghai, there are no free or reduced-fee hospitals at all. Even if there are one or two public hospitals, only people with connections can get treatment. Poor people can forget about getting in. When workers get sick, their wages are stopped, which is already a loss, but household expenses increase, and they also have to pay medical expenses, so in fact they cannot wait long. Therefore, sick workers suffer from mental and material pressure, so often a small illness becomes a major illness, a major illness becomes death, and some people relapse after their first recovery due to overwork, which is so heartbreaking! I am one of the people who are closest to female workers. Usually what I hear and see are these things, which makes me feel helpless and extremely difficult. In addition, worker unemployment is also a very important issue, so I feel that everything about labor is not a simple issue, especially in the current stage of China, which needs to be resolved urgently!"

Requesting Guidance on Birth Control

— Chengzi

I have been unemployed for almost a year because of having children.

After the child was born, I dared not delay any longer on the issue of how to practice birth control.

Accidentally, I saw at the registration desk of the hospital that the Gynecology Department had a section for guiding childbirth and controlling childbirth, the time for which was every Thursday afternoon. That day happened to be my shift, so I registered and went to the waiting room to request guidance on how to control childbirth.

There were already many people sitting in the waiting room. I didn't know if they were all there to receive education on birth control methods. When my number was called, I was called in. A girl, probably a female intern from the medical school, led me to a room inside and began to ask about my menstrual cycle, number of births, etc. I told her that everything was fine, and that it had only been three months since I gave birth to my last child. She looked at me with a look of surprise and said: "You don't want to have children? Well, wait outside for a while, the doctor hasn't come yet." As she spoke, she took another examination form and called another name. I followed her out, and many people's eyes were focused on me, as if they wanted to inquire about the news inside, but I didn't satisfy them, and I quietly sat down among them.

After that, one by one went in and out, but it wasn't my turn. After waiting for about two hours, my name was called again. A boy - I probably didn't insult him, because he didn't look like a doctor at all, although he was wearing a white coat - told me to sit down and began to ask me the reason why I wanted to practice birth control, and then asked me about my family situation and financial situation, which were all filled in on a form. After filling it out, he smiled at me and said: "You sit outside for a while, and I'll call you in later." It seemed that all the conditions for birth control had been met, which made me very happy. I happily ran back outside again.

Before long, I was called in again. This time I saw a doctor, who asked me briefly about the reason why I didn't want to have children, and then led me into the examination room. He told me to lie down on the hospital bed. The hospital bed was very high. After I lay down, the boys and girls all gathered around to watch the doctor examine me. I was very scared. I felt like I was meat on a chopping block. The doctor gave physiological instructions to the students in a foreign language, and then taught me how to use a cervical cap. The so-called cervical cap was just a thin rubber thing like a small teacup. The method of use was very simple: just put the thing completely into the vagina. The doctor also wrote a prescription and told me to buy medicine, which was placed in the cervical cap when it was used. I climbed down from the hospital bed, and the doctors all walked outside. I stood alone and straightened my clothes. At this time, the nurse had already packed the cervical cap that had just been used, and also took another bottle of toothpaste-like tin tubes, and handed one to me, saying: "Take this, it's five yuan, and the medicine is another one yuan." I couldn't help but be stunned. I happened to have six yuan on me, but this six yuan was the living expenses for the second half of the month. I really didn't dare to give it to her rashly. (I heard that in countries where birth control is publicly available, the price of a cervical cap is only about two jiao.) I told her that I didn't bring that much money. She said! "Well, come and get it tomorrow." I said, "Okay." I felt very lost when I left the hospital.

In the evening, I told my husband about what happened during the day. He said: "Go and get it. You promised others, how can you not get it?"

But I hesitated. Six yuan is a large sum for me. The next day, I didn't go to get it after all. For a woman who dare not have children because she cannot afford to raise them, this contraceptive device is too expensive. I can only let the shadow of the second child heavily weigh on my head.

Lecture on Venereal Diseases

— Co-edited by Dr. Yao Erchang, MD, USA and Dr. Zhan Nianceng, Venereal Disease Specialist

(Clinic) 2nd Floor, China Trust Company, Corner of Sichuan Road and Beijing Road (Consultation) 10:00 AM to 6:00 PM. Closed on Sundays.

Commentary

The Beihai Incident

— Me

The Chengdu incident, in which Japanese Ambassador to China Kawagoe, has just received instructions from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to prepare for talks, but unexpectedly, the Beihai incident suddenly occurred again. The continuous occurrence of such unfortunate incidents is truly a major blow to the friendly relations between the two countries, which is deeply regrettable.

How did the Chengdu incident start, and how did such serious consequences occur? A more detailed report has not been obtained at this time, so it is impossible to make a concrete judgment. However, there are several points that can be inferred: (1) Ordinary rioters disrupted local order, and Japanese reporters happened to be there and suffered misfortune, with no intention of revenge. (2) Ordinary rioters took advantage of the tense situation between China and Japan to vent their pent-up anger or to create a situation that was difficult to resolve through negotiations, making it difficult for the government to cope. However, this kind of incident occurred in the provincial capital of Chengdu, and the local authorities cannot but bear the responsibility for it. However, it is only a local incident and is generally unrelated to national relations. It should not be made a big deal out of a small issue.

As for the Beihai incident, it is even more unfortunate. Although Guangdong has now been largely pacified, the local issues in Guangxi Province are currently being negotiated, and there is a good turn for a peaceful resolution. However, the generally strong and unruly troops, who come when Li Bai calls them, cannot be dismissed as quickly as desired. These troops are still lingering in the Beihai area. At this time, they are unwilling to accept not only the orders of the central government, but also likely the orders of Li Bai. These troops, gathered in one corner, seeing no hope of a way out, fear nothing more than peace in the area, and they long for something to happen every day. They do not hesitate to create this kind of heinous crime, making things difficult for the central government. Under these circumstances, the central government has no way to protect foreign nationals, and can only hope that foreign nationals are good at taking care of themselves. Therefore, this kind of responsibility is one that our authorities do not dare to shirk, but they also cannot fully bear the responsibility for it.

In short, at a time when the negotiations between the two countries are serious, and when the negotiations between the two countries are improving, foreign nationals should be cautious and prudent, and should exercise some restraint in these unstable areas to avoid causing incidents. Because the government's protection of foreign nationals is originally a duty, but in the chaotic local situation, although there is a sincere desire to protect, the circumstances are restrictive and it is difficult to be comprehensive in a short time. This is also a helpless situation.

Moreover, this kind of incident occurs in a certain local area, either because ruffians take the opportunity to make trouble, or because undisciplined soldiers who are not under the control of the central government use this as a tool to oppose the central government. Therefore, this kind of incident is entirely local in nature, and cannot be exaggerated or expanded to be equated with the entire negotiation. Therefore, the adjustment of diplomatic relations between China and Japan is originally outside of this kind of problem, and not within this kind of problem. If this kind of incident is equated with the overall negotiation, then difficult problems will be in the aftermath.

A Pair of Pants

— Meiping

The bright moon is in the sky, the night is as cool as fire, and there was a drizzle again late in the evening. The universe seems to have been washed clean without a trace of dust. Sitting alone by the window, listening to the chirping of insects in the courtyard, the weariness that summer has given me is now like a weary traveler who has found a warm inn and is happily resting.

On such a quiet night, I should have gone to bed earlier to make up for months of insomnia, but the clock has already struck once, and I am still sitting by the window, waiting like a lover. On the table is a book that I like to read, and now it has been flipped to the last page by the gentle autumn breeze. It is an advertisement for a fashion store, with gentlemen and ladies wearing fur-collared coats walking out of that store. Yes, it is already autumn, and a cold winter is coming soon.

So I felt a chill invading my limbs, and I hurriedly put on my bathrobe, closed the window, and went to bed. My nasal passages were already slightly congested. Getting sick in the fall is also a blessing, but that fashion store advertisement is deeply imprinted on my brain. A friend who is still wearing a worn-out white canvas suit seems to have no qualifications to have a happy little illness.

I began to notice the two trunks quietly lying in the corner, as cautious as a thief. They are my only two trunks. They are my companions. From the yellow sand-swept north to the warm south, they have never left me for a second. The various luggage tags on them, like the wrinkles on my forehead, are so numerous that their exact age cannot be estimated.

What exactly is hidden in those two trunks? Even I, the owner, am a little vague, because I haven't changed the clothes I'm wearing since I moved here. That's only secondary. When I want to get a little hope from them, I can hardly even remember where to put the keys.

The trunks are covered in a thick layer of dust. I wipe them with a dry cloth, and with a little force, they make a groaning sound. Do they resent that I, the owner, am not paying attention to their health? When it rains, leaks drip down from the walls and accumulate on the bottom of the trunks. The only window in this room is so far away that they can't see any sunlight, and they only let dust and cobwebs build homes.

The trunk is open, and a musty smell rushes straight into my nostrils. In the dim light, my eyes are blurred. I can't see anything. I suspect that the trunk is empty. So, like a blind man, I reach in to feel around. I feel a few slippery things. Now I can see them very clearly. They are broken socks and smelly undershirts. I keep feeling until I reach the bottom of the trunk, and then I find the treasure: a pair of evergreen Western pants are folded and lying there. Although my sense of touch tells me that they are as greasy as loaches and covered with many white spots, my joy is indescribable. It's autumn, and I should put on autumn clothes.

But I am immediately disappointed again. What about the top? What about the vest? That suit was made in a small city, so the style is naturally not very beautiful, and the price is half as cheap as in a big city. Now, if I just go to get a top made, I'm afraid it will cost that much money, right? So I open the second trunk, because I'm too busy moving and often just pile things randomly into the two trunks before I leave. The second trunk is open again. What I pull out are broken socks and smelly undershirts, all the way to the bottom. There's nothing there.

I lie back in bed, thinking about my last move. My last move was after I was seriously ill. The expenses for medical treatment sent all my valuables to the Changsheng warehouse. And because I couldn't find the pants at the time, I only sold the top and vest of that suit. So, what am I still looking for?

The moonlight in autumn is too beautiful. It shines through that small window onto my sleeping bed, allowing me to fall asleep instinctively. But I no longer have the interest to enjoy the moon. On the contrary, I find it very annoying.

My nasal passages are still congested. I'm afraid I'll get sick tomorrow.

Companion of Love

We will love each other forever. Heaven and earth will grow old and not separate. Our love is strong. The seas may dry up and rocks may crumble, but it won't break. Love is making a big fuss inside. It says spring has arrived. Love quarrels. Love makes a fuss. The heart cannot be closed. Our hearts are full of passion. Even the Yangtze River cannot extinguish it. Heart fire burns. Heart fire jumps. The heart cannot be closed. Look at the green grass. Look at the bright moon. That is our pure and true love. Flowers smile brightly. Little stars twinkle. Flowers are my body. Stars are my heart. God turns us into one clay figure. Beaten with hammers. Burned with fire. In the future. Forever inseparable.

Afterthoughts

Every Saturday afternoon at 4:00 PM, cartoonist Zhang Yizhang's "Weekly Cartoon Lecture" is hosted by Zhongxi Radio Station. This issue's topic is "From Cartoons to Traditional Chinese Painting," divided into four sections: Section 1, "The Rise and Fall of Chinese Painting," Section 2, "The Influence of Ritual Ethics on Painting," Section 3, "The Decline and Revival of Figure Painting," Section 4, "The Contribution of the Six Principles to Cartoons." Those concerned about Chinese fine arts and art education can tune in on time.

Movie News

"Star" Volume 6, Issue 4 Published

Volume 6, Issue 4 of the Star Bi-Monthly was published yesterday. This issue has new improvements in content and form. In terms of images, the wonderful scenes from the Star Second Factory's two new works, "Life and Death Together" and "Qingming Season," are featured in this issue. A plate of "Little Lingzi" paintings, a full-page photo of Li Minghui, Orchestra is a photographic sketch of the studio work of the photo cartoon, and two elegant scenes from the new film "Night Meeting" have also been published. There are also four bi-monthly cartoons and many other cartoons by famous artists, a landscape photo "Yin" taken by Zhang Jinde, two editions of stills from Hu Die's long-awaited new work "Women's Rights," and one edition of remains from "Begonia Red." A special edition of "Qingming Season" includes the sheet music for "Worker's Song" composed by He Luting and written by Ouyang Yuqian. In terms of text, "Bi-Monthly Chit-Chat" includes Lin Zhenzhen's "The Concept of Film" and Lin Muhong's "Personnel Disputes," Hu Zhi's translation of "Crude Production and Meticulous Masterpiece," Yao Shennong's "Film," and the continuation of Chapter 3 of "The Road of Soviet Film Art." The "Reader's Tea Room" discusses "National Defense Films" and other issues. "Star March" writes about the recent work situation of the Star Company. Follow Shot is a humorous record of fragments of stars and film people. This particularly enriched issue of the Star Bi-Monthly is still priced at six cents.

"Street Running Mr."

Grand Light Screening

San Francisco Playing Continuously for Nine Days, Box Office Success Continues

Since its internal renovation, the Nanjing Grand Theater has been showing great blockbusters one after another. Last Thursday night, it premiered MGM's blockbuster "San Francisco," starring Clark Gable and Jeanette MacDonald, which has now been running for nine days. The box office is still extremely successful, with over 30,000 viewers, and there are still many who are turned away every day. It is said that the theater, in order to meet the needs of all sectors of society, has decided to continue showing the film so that movie fans at sea who have not seen it can enjoy it as soon as possible.
